### Post by lisati on 2008-10-30
Background: I'm using the "relase candidate" versions downloaded a day or two back. Here is a summary of results so far:

Laptop 1: Older Toshiba laptop, Celeron M, 256Mb ram. Previously dual boot Feisty & XP. Pretty much flawless clean install from alternate disk. Pleasantly surprised that sound worked out of the box (it didn't with Feisty, installing updates fixed that) Using the Ubuntu desktop seems sluggish at times (with disk activity noted: perhaps swapping? haven't really looked into it yet) but using the xubuntu desktop seems to be better.

Laptop 2: Fairly new Toshiba, a dual-code machine 2Gb, 64-bit. Wubi'ed install "within" Vista home premium. The only thing noted so far that needs my attention is the need of a suitable version of flash player plugins, but I'm not in a great rush to get that one sorted out.

Compaq desktop: there's something odd going on with the partitions here (resizing seems to be causing problems) so this one will have to wait. At the risk of upsetting the "Linux-only" team, this one's staying "XP only" for now.

I'll just whip off and configure samba for proper file sharing.....

### Post by cob on 2008-10-30
I downloaded the 8.10 AMD64 desktop image.  I've so far run into one fundamental problem:

I'm running an Intel ICH10R RAID-0 array with two 120GB Seagate drives.  Ubuntu's install did not correctly detect the array.

I simply pressed CTRL+ALT+F2 and ran the following:

sudo apt-get install dmraid <--- installs dmraid.
sudo dmraid -r <--- shows detected RAID arrays, they look like a long string of letters, you should see all the member drives with the same array ID.
sudo dmraid -ay (RAID ID goes here) <--- makes the RAID array active, mine was automatically activated by dmraid.

Once this was done, I hit CTRL+ALT+F7 to get back to the graphical installer, hit the back button from the partitioning menu to get back to the language/keyboard selection, then forward again, and my RAID array was then found as an install target.

This really should have been taken care of by whoever created the installer.

EDIT: Once it was done installing (or seemed to be), it booted me into the live installation on the CD.  If I were new to Ubuntu, I would have been very confused, since it did not ask me to reboot to the hard disk installation.  I was getting several errors while installing, I think because I need to reburn the CD at a lower speed, but the installation wouldn't boot (MBR problem).  Will try again after a slower CD burn.

### Post by florinn on 2008-10-30
I've upgraded from 8.04 to 8.10 on Fujitsu Siemens Esprimo Mobile v5505 Notebook

Two errors during upgrade process, cannot install python-uniconvertor and another one I don't remember
E: python-uniconvertor: subprocess post-installation script returned error exit status 1

After upgrade complete I've discovered by now the following problems

- current session is not saved, running programs are not remembered at startup
- in Firefox 3 the bookmarks toolbar if displayed is empty though there are bookmarks in it....very strange
- system seems to boot slower, run slower
- I had problems with keyboard layouts, I use three layouts, 1 English and 2 Romanians, they were not working I had to delete the Romanians and add them again
- the content of CPU Frequency Scaling Monitor Applet is not visible anymore, it appears as an empty rectangle

Problems unsolved
- same problem as before with brightness manager if display goes to sleep when it awakes the brighteness does not have the level set in power manager, it is usually greater

Maybe there are things that are not working I shall update my post if I discover new ones or if I solve current problems
So far I am not very content with the upgrade, very small benefits, I should notice the compact view and maybe tabs in Nautilus (though compact view seems primitive) and overall few graphic improvements

Update:
- CPU applet removed and added again to panel, it is working now
- Firefox reseting toolbars and rearranging them, now working
- python-uniconvertor removed (apt-get remove) and reinstalled through Synaptic without errors

Very annoying problem with sessions not saving, problem still persists

Another serious problem, system crashed twice, once when running Kstars and once again when system were idle for half an hour and I found it with a black screen and hdd working hard, no response from mouse or keyboard, I had to cut off the power (standby is not enabled on my system, only usual programs were running, so I don't know what could have caused this)

Update 2:
Meanwhile I found out that the annoying session bug is due to the new version of Gnome
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/gnome-session/+bug/249373](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/gnome-session/+bug/249373)

No more crashes, system is working fine, speed is ok.

Update 3:
Vodafone Mobile Connect is not working anymore but the modem was automatically recognized by the system and (I was very surprised) configured for my carrier, Vodafone Romania
Very good job indeed!!!

### Post by pmgeahan on 2008-10-30
I upgraded to Intrepid this morning.  I have a Dell XPS 710 that has been running Ubuntu since purchase.  First Gutsy, then Hardy, now Ibex.  The video card, a GeForce 8600 GTS, has always been a little touchy, but using Envy/EnvyNG has always worked.  Never had a problem.

Until the Intrepid update.  Absolute disaster.  The primary issue(although I'm nowhere near done yet) seemed to occur during the installation of a new kernel.  The system installed 2.6.25-2-386.  Apparently, this install required the headers and/or source to be links to 2.6.25-2.  However, it pointed them somewhere else entirely, to a place that didn't exist.  Many, many drivers failed installation because of this; thankfully, i was able to find the problem by focussing on the Nvidia driver first, since the docs said it would work for this combo.  My system only sees one CPU now, the sound card is down, and lord only knows what else is now broken that wasn't before.  A full re-install might be the best bet, but I don't know if I want to go there.  I'm not honestly quite sure how to even tell what may have failed, as several of the packages that failed failed *silently*, including the nvidia driver and alsa, so far.

---

### Post by Relysis on 2008-10-30
The upgrade went very smooth.  It was fast I think (under 2 hours from start to finish, including download).  I accepted all the changes it wanted to make along the way, as well as removing the old packages - there were almost 80 for me.  

I did have a couple problems.  If I go to Places, then select any of those folders, they all open the program EasyTag.  I have no idea why this happens.  All the places link to EasyTag now... somebody else said theirs was linking to VLC media player.  I have no idea how to fix this, but it is really annoying.  I didn't have any problems with most of my programs.  Mobloquer is being weird, I will try to reinstall it.  Something also happened to my most important application of all.... Ardour.  It says, "Failed to execute child process.. no such file or directory."  All my other audio applications still work.. I will reinstall and pray that fixes it.  Anybody else have problems with Ardour after upgrade?

I like the upgrade a lot overall though.  The new network options are great, and somehow all my graphical problems have been fixed.  I have an ATI radeon using the fglrx driver, and before there was flickering in things like google earth.  It's completely fixed now.  A couple applications also had problems with displaying video correctly, like Regnum Online, and that now works as well.  The integration of pidgin and new guest login is also a bonus for useability.

If anybody has fixed the places links, or know anything about Ardour, please let me know!

### Post by Aeterno on 2008-10-30
I had been running the intrepid beta / alpha on my notebook for some time, since it's not a critical part of my machine environment at the moment. So, in full confidence I entered the update cycle on my desktop (I know, the two are fundamentally different, but still)

All fine and dandy, around 2 hours later the update was done, and the mandatory reboot takes place, so far so good.
Immediately after the reboot however, Xorg jumps into "Low graphics mode" >_> oh joy.

Figuring this would probably be a matter of reinstalling the Nvidia drivers (new Xorg version and everything) I continue into low graphics mode to install the drivers and reboot. Easy enough.
After the reboot, Error messages pop up that the Nvidia kernel could not be initialized, and no usable screens could be found :mad:

Not discouraged quite yet, I revert back to the _older_ Nvidia drivers >_> only to find the same error. (double ugh)

I tried resetting to the default config and everything, and right now I _finally_ have one of my two monitors working at a decent resolution.
I fear it'll take another mountain or two of patience to get the other one working on my GF7900 >__>

All in all, not as smooth as I had hoped, and it's probably going to keep me up tonight trying to find out what the hell is happening.

### Post by LacteuS on 2008-10-30
Well...
What happen with the nvidia drivers ?

I have a Thinkpad with a NVidia Quadro NVS card, and the nvidia module can't be loaded at boot.

dmesg :

nvidia: Unknown parameter `NVreg_SoftEDIDs'

modprobe and /etc/init.d/nvidia-kernel won't load the driver.

I can't figure this out... :(

What is the new configuration method for intrepid ??


Edit : 

Ok, you have to remove the variable 'NVreg_SoftEDIDs' from /etc/modprobe.d/nvidia-kernel-nkc

Pfffew... :)

### Post by lemming465 on 2008-10-30
I upgraded two machines from 8.04 to 8.10rc.  In both cases *update-manager -d* worked fairly smoothly.  The second machine, an archaic compaq presario had an error in ca-certificates-java, but after the reboot, a cruft remover run, and an update things look very good.

My first experiment, on an Toshiba Satellite laptop, still has some driver issues with wireless and video.  The particular atheros wireless chip isn't supported in the kernel yet, so I'm using ndiswrapper with it.  There is some unfortunate interaction between that and wpa_supplicant; my WPA2-PSK stopped working.  If I turn off encryption on my router plain wifi works.  Basic X for stuff like web browsing on the ATI chip is OK, but there are issues with video playback.  On the beta ATI radeon driver (not yet released to the public?) installed by default video playback fails with X server errors.  An simple downgrade to the vesa driver failed when it couldn't determine the sync parameters for the LCD screen.  A downgrade to the fglrx driver can play video, but the screen stutters to black for a fraction of a second so often as to be unwatchable.  So on this hardware 8.10 regressed a bit compared to 8.04.

On the bright side, a /dev/rtc bug I reported in launchpad against the beta got fixed by the RC.

### Post by Dumdideldum on 2008-10-30
I am still not finished with update process but I must admit, that I never had run into such serious troubles during upgrades like from 8.04 to 8.10.
The Update process produced a nasty kernel panic while updating locales, which I had to fix by uncommenting all locales despite one, my main used one.
Described in this thread:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=964133](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=964133)

This might be an unelegant or dirty way, but it made it at least possible to continue the update process - still a hard way to go as I currently face another locales problem on the screen ....

Well, maybe just bad luck with my kernel panic, but for users, who arent a bit familiar with Linux a very serious and unresolvable problem.

### Post by johnnyhop on 2008-10-30

Am I leaving something out of the command line?  When upgrading from 7.04 to 7.10 and from 7.10 to 8.04 Adept Manager had a Version Update icon visible in the toolbar.

The next day: When all else fails read the instructions!  Found the instructions on the link on the Development/Installation main page followed them and most all went well.  Two curious anomalies on two different Kubuntu machines, Grub didn't update properly, it was necessary to manually edit menu.lst to boot to the current kernel and Kwrite needed to be reinstalled.  On a positive note desktop effects perform well and took note xorg.conf didn't use the previous manually entered modifications.  

From my perspective would like "Suspend to RAM" to perform properly.  With this distro the display restores properly but the sound (using a SB Live! EMU10k1 PCI card) doesn't come back up nor does the wireless USB mouse.  If I remove the mouse cable at the USB port before suspend and replace after bringing the computer out of suspend the the mouse will come up.  This leaves sound to be the most pressing issue with suspend to RAM.

Also distro upgraded two older Xubuntu machines, all appears well well with them.

I've been dabbling with Kubuntu 8.10 Beta with KDE 4.1 on a separate partition, it had many bugs at first but upgrades have taken care of them.  Not sure yet if I like KDE 4.1, it takes some getting used to.

### Post by The Pinny Parlour on 2008-10-31
Fresh install went great.  Not one issue yet... thank goodness.

Took me a whole 15-20 mins to get everything back to how I like it.

Before I installed intrepid I backed up my Docs, Pics, Vids, Desktop, Music on to an external HDD.  I then went to Place>Home>View>show Hidden files and located the .mozilla folder (firefox - /home/***/.mozilla/firefox/u0rfnr27w.default) and the .mozilla-thunderbird folder (Thunderbird - /home/***/.mozilla-thunderbird/1z4r8ik9.default  I quickly copied these to the external HDD.  

After fresh install, quickly grab Thunderbird and open it, cancel the wizard, then close Thunderbird.  (creates a profile in your home folder)  Navigate to this folder and copy your profile to it.  The existing profile rename it, (I just put a .old on the end of it).  now rename your profile you just copied over, the same as the profile you just added .old to.
Open Thunderbird and everything is ready to go.  Do the same for Firefox for the same result.

All great so far.  :)

### Post by bswilson on 2008-10-31
I started my update late at night, east coast US time yesterday (Thursday, 10/30 11:30pm ET).  The update took about 1.5 hours in total, which for me was much faster than my 8.04 upgrade last time.

I have an older nVidia GeForce 5500 video card, so I had to back off from the legacy nv driver that got automatically installed during the upgrade.  I installed [envyNG]("http://albertomilone.com/nvidia_scripts1.html") and everything was good to go.

I'm still working to fix this myself, but I noted that there's a permanent fix checked into SVN.  Just waiting for the official fix, I suppose.

Ovarall, a pretty painless upgrade, and I like the Ibex very much so far. :)

### Post by lachild on 2008-10-31
(Ahh this is the right place...)

Well I had intended to install 8.10 a couple of weeks ago and help test, and now that we have the final release I wish I had.  I have to tell you this is the buggist (if that's truly a word) version of Ubuntu I've seen so far.

Here's my experience.

All day yesterday was spent attempting to get 8.10 installed and working.  So far I have installed the system 3 times on the same computer.  That seems like a good place to start so we'll start there.  

**The Installs:**
The first install seemed to work flawlessly.  All my hardware was working and everything installed fine.  No problems here.  I did find a few major bugs in gnome that I will talk about in a second, which caused me to install KDE and try that out... That had it's own issues so I decided to simply reinstall and start over with gnome.

The second install did not go quite so well.  I went through the same steps but this time my Intel(R) Wireless WiFi Link AGN driver for Linux was not installed correctly and the wireless card was unusable.  Also using the guided "Use the entire hard drive" install did not allocate the entire drive like it should of.  Instead it only took over 3/4 of the drive.  The next problem I hit was just minor, it seems when I came up to the map to select my timezone it started in Antarctica.  Again not a big deal but since I've never had that happen before it was a little confusing none the less.  

Since the first install went fine I opted to not even attempt to figure out what happened with the second install and simply reinstalled the system again.  This time it went like the first and everything was fine.  Strange.


Where I am really running into problems is with the use of dual screens using a separate x session through an Nvidia card.  It seems that gnome has some serious problems with this right now. For instance when I attempt to use a launcher from the menu bar it causes the whole system to lock up unless you currently have a terminal window open and can restart the gnome-panel process. What I'm also seeing with dual screens is say I select an item from the Places menu from the second screen, it will always show up on the first.  Same thing is true with the volume slider that pops up from the volume icon when selected from the second screen.

There are some other annoyances in gnome that I've found.  The Calender and Evolution-alert continue to prompt me for access to the key ring even though I have selected to "Always Allow".  Evolution would not use the spell checker after an install.  To get his to work you have to un-check the spell checker, restart evolution and reselect it from the preferences menu and restart evolution for it to work correctly. 

Nvidia-settings complained about the word "Default" in the xorg.conf file.  Not sure what that was about.  This was fixed by simply allowing it to save it's own xorg.conf file without merging it with the old one.

KDE also had it's issues with the Dual Screen setup.  As a matter of fact it wouldn't even start a KDE session on the second screen at all.  X was there and I could move my mouse to it, but it had no KDE session.

KDE was also super slow on this computer.  Not sure why that is, as I installed KDE4 when I was on Hardy and never noticed that it was that much slower.  Maybe I just forgot.

That's all the issues I've hit so far, but I've only had it fully installed for about 6 hours now.   


So far I would have say this is the worst release I've personally seen come out of Ubuntu.  It actually feels more like a Fedora release then a Ubuntu release.  I know this release is to be more on the cutting edge and there will be bugs, but what I'm really worried about is when some of these show-stoppers with dual screen will be fixed.  I know when had these types of problems with Fedora I could expect a quick fix, but with Ubuntu's update schedule I am worried that I won't see a fix for these for quite some time.

Anyway, here's to hoping these issues find quick easy fixes and thanks for giving me a place to share my frustrations

LaChild

PS.  I just noticed while I was posting this that the spell checker is also not working for FireFox.  I think I'll try the same type of thing we had to do for evolution.

Edit: Disabling the Ubuntu modifications in tools and reactivating it worked.

---

### Post by jerrylamos on 2008-10-31
Any way to put a "sticky" in Installations & Upgrades?  A lot of people are getting very similar problems many of whom are helped by my reply:

subject: black or tan screen

Any number of us are having problems with 8.10 compiz. My thinkpad gets a black or tan screen instead of a desktop. The workaround in Launchpad Bug #259385 is:

boot in rescue mode
select root shell prompt
sudo apt-get remove compiz
sudo apt-get remove compiz-core
exit
resume normal boot

If later on you want to try compiz you can install it with Synaptic. As of Oct 31 update compiz still freezes my pc. The "official" fix is blacklisting some graphics hardware so that compiz won't be run on them.

Jerry

I typed in the key and now my wireless connection is working again.  Two reboots is what was needed to resolve the issue.  I'm surprised that my saved key was lost during the upgrade.

All is well now, but I still will never again use the update manager to upgrade the OS.  There's too much at stake to not test a new OS from a live CD to ensure that the essentials will function before making changes to your system.  It was a lesson well learned.

**Total Harddisk space: 500Gb**
[COLOR="Blue"]/dev/sda1  /                           10 Gb   Format ext3 
/dev/sda2  /home                       10 Gb   Format ext3
/dev/sda3  /<separate data partition> 450 Gb          ext3
/dev/sda4  swap                         5 Gb[/COLOR]

The installation was smooth.

### Post by tomward on 2008-11-01
upgrade itself "seemed" to work OK but unable to reboot
I have /boot as raid 1 and the rest as raid 0
the upgrade process removed mdadm and friends from initrd so the init scripts no longer assemle the raid 0 volume

moral 
1. is be careful doing automated upgrade with 8.10
2. having /bin /etc and /sbin on raid0 is a bad idea, silly me.

once I get the system running again I will move etc and bin and sbin to the raid 1 volume. If i had done this the first time I would have been able to rescue the system from the failsafe initramfs/busybox shell

### Post by SABCD on 2008-11-01
Hardy to Intrepid experience:

Upgrading(Friday October 31 experience):

(I keep all my data on separate partition from the operating system.  This should be considered sane practice by anyone.  I always also copy the entire working old operating system to a backup drive before attempting to upgrade.  My suggestion is  that you make sure you have some sort of restorable backup before proceeding. I uninstalled open office 3.0 before starting per other peoples postings)

1. Upgrading from the alternative cd is a total failure.  This was the same situation as going from Gutsy to Hardy.  My suggestion is don't even bother...use "Update Manager" and upgrade on-line directly from the repositories. I had to copy back the partition and start over.

2. Using "Update Manager" and upgrading directly from the repository on-line, I was able to download all files at full speed over a 7Mbps dsl connection and this took 45 minutes. (I did test in "Administration->Software Sources->Download From->other"for the best repository location.)  Installation of the files took about another hour. I would recommend going this route if at all possible. 

3.  After installing and "cleaning" out the old files, the system attempted to restart.  This appears where many people are having trouble.  Note!...it will take forever for the computer to restart...just go have a cup of coffee or something and don't touch anything during this interval.  The screen will be blank, but about every 30 seconds or so there will be a hit on the hard disk.

4. On restarting,  the system gave me a message that it was going to start the display in ...sorry forgot the exact message.... low resolution? mode....my having tried all the other choices, you should just let it boot with the "low" mode...it is booting into nv video.  (The nvidia driver driver is failing to load).  I attempted to effectively delete file xorg.conf and to follow the message you get when you attempt to start nvidia-settings but that alone did not fix the problem.  The solution was to go into Administration->Hardware Drivers, disable the nvidia driver and re-start X(control-alt-backspace).  I then went back into Hardware Drivers and re-enabled the nvidia driver and completely rebooted the machine.  This fixed the driver problem.  However, even though my .nvidia-settings.rc file was hidden in a "root" location and faked out by providing a link in my home directory, it was still over-written, and I had to reconfigure the display using nvidia-settings.

5. My sound options, including which sounds to play for system events were completely overwritten by the upgrade and had to be completely reconfigured.

6. Files that were modified during the installation which you might want to backup before starting:

	mime.types, menu.lst, (gnome) defaults.lst(I kept the old), /etc/readahead/boot, /etc.init.d/mountdevsubfs.sh, smb.conf, .nvidia-settings.rc.

7. Many compiz settings were overwritten and had to be re-configured. Might want to back up the configuration file for compiz wherever it might reside.

8. The upgrade uninstalled "slocate"...minor issue...I suppose I am one of the few who still prefers to use it.

9. I had my tools bars on firefox customized.  The upgrade totally messed up my customizations. I then could not re-customize the tool bars.  The work around was to uninstall "ubufox" and I was then able to rearrange the stuff on my tool bars, add back my bookmarks and have it be persistent. 

What's still broken:

1. It takes two minutes and 10 seconds for the machine to shut off gracefully.  I suppose this is not a big deal unless you are attempting to re-start, (and then you will inevitably hit the  reset button on the computer.)

2.  Title bars(decorators) are not always re-drawing properly, often just disappearing or drawing only partially.  

3. Pulseaudio  totally screwed up as usual. My suggestions is, don't even waste your time.  Just configure to use ALSA for everything.

4. On re-starting there seems to (still) be a bug where Glipper fails to load.  This was also happening on Hardy, but now seems to be more prevalent.  Workaround is to choose not to remove it from the panel when prompted and to then re-start X.

5.I was using s2both inside a script to suspend and that no longer works.  On resume the screen would not wake up.  I changed "s2both" to "pmi action suspend" and that seems to now work.  (The standard way of suspending using the shutdown button does work.)

6. This is an unknown.  Prior to this upgrade, I have always had this problem where occasionally the machine would suddenly just power off. It would tend to happen maybe once every three weeks or so.  It really is one of those things which there is no way to analyze why it happens, since it is so totally random, infrequent, and sudden with no logging of what could have happened. (Admittingly I live in a location where the power can be flaky.)  However since upgrading, I have now had this happen three times in the past day.  Has this happened to anyone else?


Positives:
1. Previous boot time (not including post) was 1 minute 30 seconds.  Now boots in 1 minute 5 seconds.
2. Some applications at least seem be running noticeably faster. However, firefox seems to be a little slower starting up.
3. New tab and compact view in Nautilus is useful.
4. Media players seem be working better.

---

### Post by seoras on 2008-11-01
After what seemed like a normal upgrade process, I was asked to OK the removal of obsolete packages, OK I said, this is normal, until I noticed the system was removing over 900 packages including Firefox, OOo, Evolution, Rhythmbox etc. Alarm bells started ringing but by then it was too late and I hoped these packages were simply being replaced. Not so, on reboot I go stuck on a blank screen displaying *Running local boot scripts (/etc/rc.local)* After searching the forums I found [others had the same problem ]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=963774") Running the following got me back to the Gnome Desktop

Ctrl Alt F1 to get to a logon terminal screen
sudo dhclient eth0 (to get network access)
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get upgrade
sudo apt-get dist upgrade

Unfortunately it would appear that most of my default packages including Open Office, Firefox, Thunderbird, Network Manager, etc. etc. had been removed. I also lost all CompizFusion eye candy. I proceeded to reinstall all my missing packages and finally tried to get my CompizFusion cube back. I have an ATI Radeon X600 video card so I installed the xorg-driver-fglrx and rebooted. DAMN !! could not get the Gnome desktop again and was left hanging at a blank terminal screen. Removed xorg-driver-fglrx and rebooted. At least I'm back to the desktop now.

This has been the most catastrophic upgrade I have ever encountered and I have been using Ubuntu since 5.04. I am going to do a clean install of 8.04.1 and will not go near 8.10 again as it appears to have a VERY serious flaw look at this poll Admittedly, many who have had a trouble free upgrade will not come to the forum to vote but a lot of people are having trouble with this upgrade.

### Post by luvr on 2008-11-01
Running into what looks like [Bug #260001: ubiquity crashed with InstallStepError in configure_bootloader()]("https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/ubiquity/+bug/260001")

So, cannot even **install** succesfully, let alone run.

I have gotten to the point that I'm beginning to understand where at least a *part* of the problem is located: It looks like GRUB doesn't want to get installed to the Boot Block of a partition--it desparately **needs** to go onto a Master Boot Record.

Now, I remember that GRUB displays a warning message when you install it onto a Boot Block (instead of a Master Boot Record)--something about an error trying to write something to disk, but it adds that this is not fatal. *(I think it must have something to do with GRUB stage 1.5, which--I think--is supposed to go to the first track of the harddisk, assuming that you install GRUB onto an MBR. However, that space is unavailable if you install GRUB onto a Boot Block of a partition.)* Seems to me that the installer encounters this warning message, and *"promotes"* it into an error.

In fact, I have just completed an install, with GRUB going onto the Master Boot Record of my *second* harddisk (which Ubuntu 8.10 treats as the *first* harddisk, by the way). With a little trickery, I can now get the Intrepid Ibex to boot, but it involves selecting the second harddisk (according to how the BIOS sees them) as the boot disk whenever I want to run 8.10.

### Post by telegram.sam on 2008-11-02
Thanks to all you early adopters out there for helping improve Ubuntu. For those of you who are stressed out by the process, and don't want the hassle (like me), there are two simple rules:

1 Don't install immediately a new version comes out, wait at least a couple of weeks.

2 Don't upgrade, do a clean install. There are infinitely more possible (software) situations for an upgrade, than for a clean install, therefore infinitely more possibilities of problems - reduce the likelihood!   

For those of you who say it should work on release - you're right, but it's software, and we don't live in a perfect world! Accept things as they are, not as you'd like them to be.

---

### Post by pmsumner on 2008-11-02
I've had 2 key problems which would prevent your average end-user from proceeding any further.

Once again, Atheros driver problems.  This time I don't think related to the kernel modules though.  I was getting kernel panics on boot, just as X started loading and I noticed that ath_pci was listed there.  I also noticed while in Rescue mode, wicd was still installed.  Removed wicd, and voila it worked like a charm.

Also had problems with Network Manager not being able to take charge of the network interfaces.  The network worked fine, and connected but only because wicd had done the work and left /etc/network/interfaces all set up right.  Once I commented out everything but lo, eth0, ath0 and wlan0 network manager was able to take control and connect as expected.

### Post by --phs on 2008-11-02
Not sure what happened to the sticky post allowing folks to vote on the upgrade, but I wanted to relay another positive experience with the Ubuntu upgrade process.

Back when I had to do lots more work on Windows, I never would have dreamed of doing anything other than clean installs for OS upgrades.  This conclusion was reached after much trial and mostly errors...

Now, Windows is rarely used here because Linux has vast advantages over Windows for the work that needs to be done.

After starting out with Ubuntu 6.10 (?) a ways back, and upgrading 4 different machines all the way through 8.10, this has been the easiest upgrade ever here.

The most annoying problem was that downloading updates for the first machine was slow due to (I presume) lots of traffic on Ubuntu servers, even though I selected a University server near my location in the US.  Of course, this is actually a good thing in the sense that Ubuntu's popularity seems solid.

It's a nice advancement that NVidia users are somewhat handheld through the process of installing a driver with proper 3D support, which I rely upon for modeling and CAD work.

Congratulations to the Ubuntu team on another superior release!

-- phs

### Post by alanmilne on 2008-11-02
Having started with Ubuntu by doing a clean install of Hardy 8.04 on two systems ( a desktop and a laptop ) some months ago, this was my first experience of an upgrade. I have been impressed with 8.04 and others have accused me of being somewhat evangelical about it, so I decided to approach the upgrade from the position of someone who is [COLOR="Red"]*not*[/COLOR] computer literate. 

To check out the procedure I decided to upgrade the desktop first as it was not an *[COLOR="Blue"]important[/COLOR]* system and is dual booted with Windows. This would allow me access to the Internet even if things went wrong and proved to be a [COLOR="Blue"]wise[/COLOR] move!! Over the years I have also learnt the value of system backups so had the complete image on a handy USB stick. I also had CDs of the desktop install and the alternate install just in case.

As this was experimental I decided to do what any newbie would do and followed the *[COLOR="Blue"]recommended[/COLOR]* procedure as laid out on the website, so I started the Distribution Upgrade and waited to see what happened. Boy did it take a long time!! There was no indication of how long this would take (during the cleaning phase) or of what was going on. If I had not seen that the disk activity light was flashing away I could have assumed that the system had crashed.

When the upgrade finished and the system rebooted, guess what? It did not come back properly and was stuck at the gnome start-up procedure (reading /etc/rc.local [OK]). Luckily I was able to boot Windows and access Ubuntu Forums to discover that many people were having the exact same experience.

To get around this I completely rebuilt the system with 8.04 (from my backup) and decided to try again. Then I read the release notes!! I had not reconfigured the keyboard and mouse away from Xorg control.:oops:

Having reconfigured the keyboard and mouse, I decided to try the upgrade from the alternate install CD instead. I elected not to use the internet for this procedure and all appeared to be going well until I received several screens indicating problems with libxslt and libxml2 and suggesting that I submit bug reports about this (just what a newbie [COLOR="Red"]*does not*[/COLOR] want to see)!!

When the system eventually rebooted there was some interesting messages about incomplete software, etc. so I started update manager to see if I could solve this. Eventually I was prompted to perform another 'Partial upgrade' and this appears to have solved most of the issues.

This has lead me to what I feel are some relevant points:-

[LIST=1]
[*]I should have read the release notes before starting!!
[*]Without access to another system I would *[COLOR="Red"]not[/COLOR]* have been able to access the internet and find solutions to the problems I was having. I would have been stuck with an unusable system!!
[*]Would it not have been possible to ensure that the 'keyboard/mouse' issue was addressed in the upgrade procedure?
[*]Whilst a lot of the advice given in Ubuntu Forums is very good, it is written by those who like to 'tinker under the hood'. People who just want their computer to work may not understand the advice or may feel incapable of following it.
[/LIST]

With many years of experience in the computer industry my own instinct is to perform a clean install but I should point out again that I *[COLOR="Blue"]deliberately[/COLOR]* approached this from a newbie's point of view.

I am still very impressed with Ubuntu and feel that those behind it have achieved a lot and should be thanked. My comments are simply aimed at trying to improve the experience of users and to move Ubuntu to the top of the operating system league table (no flame wars please).

---

### Post by petermck on 2008-11-02
Pretty good upgrade really. I went from Hardy Heron to Intrepid with only a couple of minor issues.
Initially it failed saying there was a problem most likely caused by third party packages or a pre-release install and to check the log. There was a problem with postgresql-plperl 8.2, which appears to not be available for Intrepid. I un-installed that package and the installation proceeded without any further issues.
When I rebooted it did not shut down properly hanging with a message "killed" "fail" on the screen until I did a hard shut down.
It did something similar at the next two shutdowns and appeared to hang while trying to stop the alsa driver, but now it shuts down cleanly.
No problem booting except the process is slower that 8.04 was.
I had to reinstall my printers because I chose to replace the cupsd.conf file during the upgrade, but cups is so easy to use now it only took 5 minutes to do.
I had to re-enter the SSID and passphrase for my wireless network before nm-applet would pick it up, but after that no problems.
Everything else seems to work fine. I've been using Ubuntu since Dapper and it's come a long way. This would be the easiest upgrade so far.
The developers and Canonical deserve a great deal of thanks for the good work.

### Post by rlgoddard on 2008-11-02
Hi,

I upgraded from Hardy to Intrepid.  It works almost flawlessly.  Only two problems that were quite easy to fix:  the screen resolution was set at a high number with panning turned on (solved using nvidia settings on my nVidia GeForce 6200A and saving the settings to the X11.conf file) and the double tray icon on wicd (solved by removing the autostart entry -- now shows only one icon).  I also had a problem not loading up the boot menu, but Kubuntu somehow solved it all by itself the second time I booted.  My RT2500 wireless card was recognized right out of the box, complete with the previously installed wicd.  I'm impressed so far!

FYI, during the upgrade procedure, I told it to overwrite all config files and clean up old software.

Something to do soon -- switch over to using ndiswrapper to run the RT2500 wireless card.  Link quality is all over the chart with the supplied rt2500pci driver. I previously used ndiswrapper in Hardy to stabilize the connection and get a faster connection.

Take care,
Russ

### Post by silkstone on 2008-11-02
Blimey, I'm really pleased I looked at this thread and the many others that relate to Intrepid upgrade problems.

I've never liked Canonical's policy of reinventing the wheel every six months, but I believe they should look at the whole subject again in the light of people's experiences here.

I'm not a computer nerd - I just want a stable and usable alternative to Windows. Hardy provides that quite well, except that I'm left with old versions of bundled software even though new releases would probably work.

The reports on problems upgrading to Intrepid are very discouraging. Even before all the bugs are ironed out of the previous version, along comes a new one with even more bugs of its own. Sorry folks, but this is no way to win support for Ubuntu or Linux. Vista provided an opportunity to persuade people to shift to a stable and more efficient alternative, instead of which we want them to jump through hoops every six months just to keep the OS up-to-date. It's a great shame.

### Post by noctiphile on 2008-11-02
I upgraded Ubuntu.  It went really well except for a couple of related things.

With 8.04 I had trouble finding support for a new monitor I installed.  I eventually solved the problem by installing NVIDIA proprietary drivers for my GeForce2 GTS chipset, available in the Ubuntu repository.  After that I chose my hardware and settings using displayconfig-gtk, which was in the Administration menu.  8.10's version of X.org apparently didn't support that driver anymore so it was removed during the upgrade.  My display was stuck in low resolution and the tool I used before, displayconfig-gtk, is also no more in Ubuntu (8.10).

I followed the instructions that an Ubuntu Developer posted and added resolutions I new to be valid, to the Screen section of my new, bare, xorg.conf file.  That didn't help anything.

I went back to a solution I posted before to get it working.  I added a kernel boot parameter to the appropriate line in my /boot/grub/menu.lst file.  The one I wanted was vga=792.  That changed the panel size to 1024x768, which is what my card/monitor combo supports.  [This]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=743471") details what I did before.

Something I did not try is to download another NVIDIA driver set of packages I found with Synaptic, for 8.10.  Perhaps doing that, enabling the driver using Hardware Drivers, and changing xorg.conf as above would have worked as well.

---

### Post by eks on 2008-11-02
Had many problems with wifi. It was not working and spent a few days trying to bring it up again: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6089169&postcount=3](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6089169&postcount=3)

In short, to make wifi work on Hardy I had to install madwifi driver manually. Which broke occasionally on kernel updates, which was the reason I was waiting for Ibex anxiously.

The upgrade broke wifi, but I didn't wanted to install madwifi driver again. After much research, I've found out that, PROBABLY, the previous installation of madwifi driver had left a /etc/modprobe.d/madwifi that blacklisted ath5k, which was the driver being used on linux-backports-modules-intrepid. Commenting that and blacklisting ath_pci and ath_hal did the trick.

But I still am curious to know what are each of this 3 and where they come from...

---

### Post by zengrits on 2008-11-02
Installed Ubuntu 8.10 on an old Sotec 3120 with Celeron 1.2 processor, 384 mb of ram and SIS audio and video.

I can't think of a superlative worthy of this operating system on the aging laptop, which crawled with the original operating system, Windows XP. How about awesome, stupendous, divine, amazing.

The install was flawless and I was immediately able to connect wirelessly using a Office Depot Aptiva 54G PC card (Atheros chipset). This lappy is too old to have a built-in wireless card.

During my trial with a CD, I was able to set up a mobile connection using my Alltel Kyocera KPC650 PC card. That time I went into networking and picked the AT&T option, but plugged in my Alltel connection info. It worked fine.

Ubuntu was my distro of choice a few years ago, but the last few versions seemed problematic on my various laptops. So I opted for some other versions of Linux.

The latest - 8.10 - has turned an obsolete computer into a dream machine. My Aspire One with XP is sitting in the closet unused. It's much more pleasant to use the Sotec with 8.10, although I'm sure I'll get back to the Acer.

Used guided partitioning last time I installed.  Filled most of my disk through use of 804.  Had to back up a lot of data and ended up losing a VM and also all previous data because of guided partitioning.

Scans of mirror for APT took a very long time but I suspect that it was because of upgrading frenzy going on across the world while I installed.  Compiz works beautifully with my Dell.

IBM machine upgraded as well.  It uses ATI X300 and still cannot run compiz though it may be due to my very high choice of screen resolution (3600x1400 dual monitor config).  

I'd say my greatest headache was not with Ubuntu but rather VMWare.  I am using VMWare player now because the latest version of VMWare server is ridiculous.  They have apparently replaced the standard windowed interface with a web-based one running in a tomcat container.  Also vmware player seems to want to start up DHCP servers for its vmnet adaptors.  I had to reconfigure dhcp conf file in /etc/vmware not to use dhcp for fear that my machine would mess up the company network...

### Post by neutro on 2008-11-02
I share the pain of the people for which the upgrade was not so successful: it happened to me a few times before. Of course that kind of poll/thread is self-selective: people with a grudge are more likely to vote than others.

So I must say, I was surprised everything was fine and top notch for me on two computers (a custom desktop system with a core 2 duo, but dual-screen using the nVidia drivers, and a notebook -- nc6120 from HP/Compaq).

I was surprised than even the nvidia driver installed through Envy before the update would escape this update unharmed. I really like the new icons, logout/user switch procedure, guest session; everything is more polished.

On the laptop I feared for the wireless but everything was fine. Well, I had a dual ubuntu/kubuntu desktop and tried to uninstall as many KDE components as I could before the update, but I forgot knetworkmanager and it got the lead before the gnome network manager could start up for some reason. I just uninstalled it and the networkmanager-applet started ok at the next login.

On my 1920x1200 LCD, I was disappointed that the default wallpaper was only 1440x900 (tiled). But at least the elephant skin one is 2049x1536 and looks great.

### Post by rusty.hinge on 2008-11-02
Howdy

Upgraded from Kbuntu KDE 4.1 Hardy to Ibex on my AMD64 desktop.  

Upon reboot went to "Low graphics mode" decided to reinstall the nvidia drivers but stumbled of the Static IP problems for a bit seems I had networking but no Domain Name Services (DNS).  I manually edited the /etc/reslov.conf rebooted and something over wrote my changes.  Entered the DNS addresses in the new network connection widget no help.  I then found on the form where static IP was a known problem I changed my network to dynamic and could use my browser again.  

following the instructions on the Forum I repeatedly installed the nvidia drivers set the active driver and reboot.  No help, still low resolution and the same display was copied on both monitors.  I finally discovered I was still running an older kernel 2.6.24-19 Grub had not been updated with the new Kernel information.  I opened the /boot/grub/menu.lst copied it to a backup and manually edited it to add the new Kernel 2.6.27-7.  rebooted and whahoo the nvidia drivers worked.  

I went through a period where my DVD drives are not being mounted. I confirmed the old Kernel did mount the drives correctly as did Gnome with the new kernel.  When I re logged in with KDE the drives were present.  Not sure if it was because I had disks in the drives this time or not.  More shall be reveled 

This has not been as seamless as upgrades I've done before.  Admittedly this is the first time I upgraded directly to Kbuntu.  Don't know if that would make a difference

Rusty

### Post by hellion0 on 2008-11-03
I'll admit, my upgrade to Intrepid has been a mixed bag of sorts.

Let's start with the bad news:

First off, when I upgraded from UbuntuStudio 7.10 to 8.04, the only thing that broke was Compiz, but the laptop itself remained usable. I decided to take the plunge and upgrade again to 8.10. After the upgrade, things started breaking. My onboard wireless (a Prism 2.5 Wavelan chipset) was failing to find my router. Oh, it was connecting, but it just couldn't find anything. To add insult to injury, the system would soft-lock up either about 5 minutes after booting up, or if I attempted to try in any way to disable the onboard wireless.

I resorted to my last Hardy kernel, and it works, but it's a dirty fix. I'd much rather be able to use the new kernel instead of having to deal with regressions. I'm also not quite good enough with Linux to build a working kernel from scratch.

I guess there's a little bit of good news, however. For one, my ATI graphics didn't break in the upgrade. For another, it runs cooler, even under the older kernel.

Still, Intrepid most definitely feels like a step back. I won't be upgrading my other machines to it anytime soon.

---

### Post by adam_kimber on 2008-11-03
> **MKlemm said:**
> 
- The GUI upgrade tool crashed right in the middle of installing the downloaded packages.

Whee join the club. 

My upgrade experience was sheer hell. 

1) The GUI upgrade tool crashed whilst installing packages. (This This caused errors on the filesystem)
2) The GUI would not restart so I restarted the computer. 
3) The computer restarted but could not fix the boot partition, fsck had to be run manually. 
4) Restarted again to get machine running but this time kernel panics with the .27 kernel. 
5) Restarted with the older kernel but the package for the nvidia driver had been upgraded and no longer worked with the old kernel
6) Command line execution of apt-get upgrade resulted in dpkg moaning that previous pacakges had not been installed properly. sudo apt-get install -f worked for a few packages and then dpkg segfaulted. 
7) Could not get dpkg to restart so I rebooted. 
8) Update process had overwritten my menu.lst incorrectly and grub was trying to boot from the wrong partition. Manually edited and got the old kernel running again.
9) Repeat steps 6-8 several times after several segfaults and many problems
10) Finally get it to finish the upgrade but it did not load the proprietary driver. The proprietary driver GUI did not list my nvidia driver, so I manually installed that but then GDM would not start even in low graphics mode.
11) I gave up, flattened and reinstalled. My home is on a seperate partition in case of unrecoverable errors. 
12) Install was flawless and everything works fine now!

### Post by themusicwave on 2008-11-03
I had some serious update woes on my Dell Inspiron E1505.  At the end of the update I told it to remove "obsolete packages"  I then got this sinking feeling as it seemed to be removing everything, but I figured it knew what it was doing...

Upon reboot, Gnome wouldn't display.  I switched to a termal with alt+F3 and started trying to startx.  It told me it was missing vesa, my mouse and touchpad modules.  It also didn;t seem to be connected to the network.  Reconfiguring X was no help.

It did however see my external hard drive.  Using this I was able to backup all those files I should have backed up previously from the CLI.  

After backing up I did a fresh install and everything works perfectly.

I would give the update an F, it was the worst I have experienced since I started using Ubuntu back at Breezy Badger.

The clean install I would give an A, worked perfectly.

### Post by lifestream on 2008-11-03
Update was fine, but sound did not work, so I thought. Every time I played something, all I could hear was static. 
I ran it for a few days like that.

So I thought I would be smart, and did a fresh install. Same problem with the sound, but guess what? The problem was that the PCM volume control (not master) was set all the way to the bottom, so obviously, no matter how much I upped Master, nothing would play :P So I put PCM up, and there we go, it works :D

I got no issues whatsoever, Ubuntu boots in 40 seconds, 20 second improvement. Applications run jsut as fast I think (which is quite fast).

I'm happy.

However:
I downloaded the Kubuntu CD just out of curiosity, and it doesn't show any partitions when it asks me to format. *shrug* glad I didn't really want to install Kubuntu anyways :P

I just can't help but LOL @ those who are complaining about updates and installing from network disc is too slow. ROLF! Give it a month, or use apt-p2p. Ubuntu servers are going to be slow for quite awhile since Intrepid is a new release :-) OR DOWNLOAD UBUNTU FROM THE TORRENTS! If you're not sure, ask how!

### Post by urugTON on 2008-11-03
I have a few week old Vostro 1510 laptop which dual boots Vista and 8.04.  This weekend I added 8.10.  I do have my /home in its own partition and I had enough free space for 8.10 to have its own partition.  I did some research on grub and having multiple linux on the same drive.  

The actual installation was anticlimactic.  The only "tricky part" was selecting manual partioning, specifying the existing /home mount point and setting up a new partition for /.  

The 8.10 installation process took care of everything else.  I was pleasantly surprised at how smoothly the partitioning went and that grub needed no manual attention after the fact.  My two Ubuntus share /home without complaint.  Vista booted without protest.

So far, 8.10 has worked very well.  Much to my surprise it configured my Intel 3945 wireless connection with only the passkey for my WPA connection.  Getting that connection to work on 8.04 took several days of research for this newbie.  All else seems to work fine, but I'm not a terribly demanding user either.

For me the upgrade/install went very smoothly once I got the .iso downloaded.  That was trying, but I guess the servers were suffering from terminal popularity the first weekend that 8.10 was available.  I did manage to get the .iso through torrent.

In a bit, I’ll add 8.10 to my desktop.  FWIW, I’m not planning to ever do an upgrade in place.  There are just too many variables to contemplate.  I’m pleased that I can have two releases running side by side.  I intend to follow this approach in the future.

My congratulations to all the folks that got 8.10 working.

---

### Post by IanWood on 2008-11-03
I have upgraded two machines to 8.10, one my work one and one a home one.

Both upgrades worked ok, but I have had issues with both.

The work one has a Matrox card and the OS itself upgraded fine, BUT the drivers for the Matrox card from the Matrox site no longer work, so I can't get dual head working. I have done a bit of a look and other people have had similar problems. There seems to be an active Linux Matrox community site but I haven't time to mend it now. I get the gist that its a problem with the version of XORG. 

The home machine has a NVIDIA card and dual head still works for that. The only problem I have found so far is that Hotmail no longer seems to work -  I can real emails but not reply. Weather that's M$ checking for non Windoze machines or what I don't know. Also Opera runs really slowly now. 

I think I will reinstall 8.04, at least at work. I wanted to have tabbed Nautilus, but not at the expense of Dual Head.

Cheers

Ian

### Post by slakkie on 2008-11-03

vmware server is most probably due to an update of your kernel. That has "nothing" to do with the upgrade to 8.10. Any kernel update will make your vmware server unworkable. ### Post by jlvillaveces on 2008-11-03
Everything looked fine until it restarted.  When the welcoming screen was on, the keyboard and the mouse were inactive.  I could enter the text mode by doing alt-ctr-f1.  
I found an /etc/X11/xorg.conf file with most options inactive.  
I tried some changes with no result.  
Then I realized that in the /etc/X11 diretory there was an xorg.conf.200806.... file that had been created at the moment when the installation began.  
I copied this file to xorg.conf and everything seems to be OK now.

;)

### Post by warped0ne on 2008-11-03
AFarris01,

Does your brother's PC have an Nvidia graphics card?  There were notes about the RC causing some problems with some Nvidia cards because of the default settings or something.  I'm not real sure how to fix it, but you could check, during boot, if you still have the old kernel installed.  Press escape when it's counting down and then try to select the older kernel.  

Alternatively, you could boot into Ubuntu's "Safe Mode" and try to run the update-manager from the command prompt (sorry for the Windows terminology, I work on a XP machine 9 hours a day, and only get to spend about 2 or 3 on Ubuntu).  Once you get logged in (not sure, but you may have to log in as root), type **sudo update-manager**, I think that will initiate the update manager from that mode.

Hey guys, if I'm wrong, please correct me.

### Post by persistentstubborn on 2008-11-04
Upgrade to 8.10 messed network configuration permanently

After the upgrade to 8.10 (and sudo apt-get purge ffmpeg winff which I fetched from medibuntu repositories) my network, having being set up during 8.04 from DHCP, involving internal nameserver, timeserver & firewall/gateway as well as static private IP address of the Ubuntu workstation was messed up. Every time the workstation rebooted, /etc/resolv.conf was purged
```
lazar@milinko:~$ cat /etc/resolv.conf
# Generated by NetworkManager
```

/etc/network/interfaces containing proper network card configuration wasn't read at all, while my ethernet device (eth0) wasn't configured.

So every time the workstation rebooted I needed to
```
root@milinko:/home/lazar# pico /etc/resolv.conf
# Generated by NetworkManager
nameserver 192.168.0.21
nameserver 192.168.0.121
root@milinko:/home/lazar# /etc/init.d/networking restart
 * Reconfiguring network interfaces...                                           * Stopping the Firestarter firewall...
   ...done.
 * Starting the Firestarter firewall...
   ...done.

```

and network worked only after that.

The fix was

```
lazar@milinko:~$ sudo apt-get remove --purge network-manager-gnome network-manager
```

### Post by von Stalhein on 2008-11-04
I had a couple of issues, but I ended up OK and much better educated ;) Machine is my build, and dual boots with XP Home.

I lost the GUI after the upgrade from 8.04 to 8.10
I only had the CLI.

After some research, and help from the pros, this is how I got it back:

```
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install --reinstall ubuntu-desktop xorg xserver-xorg xserver-xorg-input-all -y
sudo mv /etc/X11/xorg.conf /etc/X11/xorg.conf.backup
sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg

```

I also had the kinit No resume image issue, which I found a fix for by

```
sudo swapoff /dev/sda5
```
(sda5 being my swapfile), then
```
sudo mkswap /dev/sda5

```
then
```
sudo update-initramfs -u
``` Apparently the UUID was different in intramfs than what the system was looking for.

The only other thing I had to do was edit /boot/menu/grub.lst after I re-installed the 2.6.27-7 kernel through Synaptic. 

I think it all came about as I answered some of the choices wrong during the upgrade process. 

This was the most troublesome u/g fro me out of the last three distros. However, as I said, I'm much better at the CLI now :)

### Post by baruch60610 on 2008-11-04
I was seriously disappointed by this upgrade.  It took over six hours to download more than 2 G of stuff, perform the upgrades, and clean up the system.  My Evolution lost data because the program had changed database options for some reason.  Many of my customizations in various programs disappeared, even though I chose to *keep* any configuration files when asked about them.

Once my upgrade was finished, I found that my display manager wanted to come up in low-res mode, because some other configuration had been lost.  My system ran incredibly slowly, for no reason I could discern.  The main hog seemed to be knotify4, which took over 50% of the cpu time.  When I killed it, the system got faster, but not as snappy as it was under 8.04.  During the upgrade, there were several points where I got an error message saying that some script didn't exist, pleas file a bug report.  When I dutifully tried to file the report, the bug reporting system failed.  So much for that idea.

I am seriously tempted to get the 8.04 installation disk and just revert back to Hardy.  This would mean I'd lose all my customized configurations, but guess what?  Already happened.  It would only take me 30 minutes to do the install, plus however long it was to choose the programs I preferred.  If I backed up my hidden directories, I could probably restore the whole thing to close to what I had before.

I see no good reason for this upgrade.  The main changes appear to be cosmetic, not functional.  I would gladly trade the flashy display stuff for more responsiveness, and to get my old customizations back.

For example, I had a second panel on the left side of the screen, where I kept shortcuts to various programs I used often.  I did this because my screen is extra-wide and I can easily spare the space on each side.  KDE4 doesn't appear to allow you to put a panel on the sides, but only at the top or bottom.  I don't have the space to spare there, so this isn't useful for me.  This is just one of the many changes that are not helpful.

I use several desktops.  In order to keep them straight, I had each one with a different wallpaper.  Just by looking at the wallpaper I could tell which desktop I was on.  Not a huge issue, but useful.  I don't find a way to do this in KDE4.  Even if it exists, I shouldn't have to dig around so hard to find it.

As I said, I wouldn't have done this upgrade, if I had known how much damage it would do to my system.  Moreover, I wouldn't install Intrepid even as a new install, because of the problems I mentioned.

My guess is that the Ubuntu folks were trying to keep to their six-month schedule, and pushed some things out that they shouldn't have.  And I probably should have waited a few weeks to let the bugs work themselves out.

I love Linux, and Ubuntu is still the best distribution around, in my opinion.  However, Intrepid is certainly not worth the hassle and the damage it did to my system.  I'm probably just going to reinstall 8.04 and consider this a lesson learned.  A harsh lesson...

### Post by dci-Japan on 2008-11-05
Installing Ubuntu 8.10 [Errno 5] My Success Story

My solution to [Errno 5] on Ubuntu install was to remove some RAM modules.

I had great trouble installing 8.10 to my computer (model: HP d330). It took me three days and countless hours researching around the internet. Here is my success story.

I downloaded the ISO and attempted to install from the Live CD. The following error appeared at about 24% of install process:

[Errno 5] Input/output error

This particular error is often due to a faulty CD/DVD disk or drive, or a faulty hard disk. It may help to clean the CD/DVD, to burn the CD/DVD at a lower speed, to clean the CD/DVD drive lens (cleaning kits are often available from electronics suppliers), to check whether the hard disk is old and in need of replacement, or to move the system to a cooler environment.

1. Attempted reburn CD-R at slower speed. Same error.
2. Attempted install with "Alternate CD". Same problem (it froze up somewhere in "copy files to disk" process).
3. Attempted boot from Live CD and double click "Install". NO GO. Wouldn't even start process.
4. Repeated all the above in various ways. Same results.
5. Tried changing the various choices under F6 on boot-up. Freeze or same error. 
6. Live CD then begin to hang on boot from CD. Couldn't get anything to do anything.
7. Attempted to install from Flash card (using separate PC to set it up). Booted fine, but same error on install.
8. Attempted many solutions offered on various forums online. Still no luck.
9. Tried noapic options and others to no avail.
10. Tried repartitioning hard drive, and wiping hard drive and etc. etc. etc.
11.Gave up and installed Windows XP. Hated it (as usual). Waited several hours. Kept repeating all the above plus anything I could think of. Redownload ISO. Burn at slower speeds. Try Alternate CD. Try Flash card again. NO LUCK. Fiddle with various settings again.

And then I used the little grey cells in my head (as Poirot would say in an Agatha Christie novel). I remembered someone somewhere suggested RAM error as the culprit. I ran the memory test without a problem (that took many hours!), but still I was supicious about the memory. My PC has four memory slots but with 3 actually memory sticks. 256Mb (original memory stick that came with computer) + 1Gb (cheap no brand stick added later) + 1GB (another added no brand stick). I simply took out the two 1Gb stick and left only the original 256Mb stick and attempted an install. Bang! It worked. No error. No problem (except it was as slow as molassis to install...). After the successful install, I replaced the 2Gb of memory and rebooted. Everything worked out. RAM modules might be faulty but everything seems fine.

I'm not sure if this solution will help everyone. The cause of [Errno 5] might be different for each machine, and sometimes just trying a million attempts leads to an eventual success. But in my case, removing most of the RAM solved the problem. 

Finally I can get on with enjoying Ubuntu 8.10.

---

### Post by Hobgoblin on 2008-11-05
Upgraded on an IBM Thinkpad R40 from Hardy.

The only problem I had was with the wireless connection.  It would connect once but then needed the connection deleting from network manager and recreating or it would just keep asking for the WPA key over and over.

I have the following WiFi card.
       product: AR5212 802.11abg NIC
       vendor: Atheros Communications Inc.


Solved by installing linux-backports-modules-intrepid-generic, then switching the driver to "Support for 5xxx series Atheros 802.11 wireless LAN cards" under system > administration > Hardware drivers.

Rebooted, and now it seems to be working fine.

### Post by allenb on 2008-11-05
I upgraded from 7.10 (Gutsy) to 8.04 (Hardy) and then immediately to 8.10 (Intrepid) using the alternative CDs and the update manager's "new distribution" button.  Downloading the CD images was much faster than I expected and the upgrade process, while time consuming, went relatively pain-free.  I haven't poked around too much since the upgrade, but there doesn't seem to be any major issues (just a couple of graphical glitches and one or two outdated applications being auto-removed).

The only complaint I have is the way the updater handles a mounted CD image.  For whatever reason, copying the updates from the alternate disc went almost twice as fast on my first leg of the upgrade (Gutsy->Hardy) than on the last leg (Hardy->Intrepid), even though the first leg used a physical CD and the last leg used a mounted CD image.  Normally, I would expect the mounted CD image to be a lot faster than an optical drive.

### Post by cdtech on 2008-11-06
I had a few problems with the upgrade myself and although my solutions worked for me they may not work for you. Please don't think of this as a fix for your own problems but as a possible direction to your own solutions.

When I did the upgrade my computer locked up during the setup (but luckily after all packages where downloaded). I had to get to a command line (a boot to CLI) and issue the command:
**sudo dpkg –configure –pending**
which finished the setup of downloaded packages and installed the new kernel (2.6.27-7).

Although this configured the downloaded packages I still had to boot into the newly installed kernel and redo the dpkg thing as above. I just stopped the GRUB bootloader and edited the kernel line to replace with the new kernel image.

I lost my **compiz** and thought I was in for a long problem solving issue when I found it to be restablished by running the “Compiz Fusion Icon”.

My **keyboard** directional arrows and multimedia buttons where inoperable. By setting the keyboard model as Generic Evdev-managed keyboard in System > Preferences > Keyboard (in the tab Layouts) corrected this for me.

I'm still working on the suspend and hibernate issues......

Hope this helps someone else........

---

### Post by rakris on 2008-11-06
> **el7azeen said:**
> How can I do it?
thanks in advance

I've already added these lines to /boot/grub/menu.lst

title		Ubuntu 8.04.1, kernel 2.6.27-7-generic
root		(hd0,4)
kernel		/boot/vmlinuz-2.6.27-7-generic root=UUID=4c66da14-93b0-4d1c-85eb-dbaf1e28b836 ro quiet splash
initrd		/boot/initrd.img-2.6.27-7-generic
quiet

title		Ubuntu 8.04.1, kernel 2.6.27-7-generic (recovery mode)
root		(hd0,4)
kernel		/boot/vmlinuz-2.6.27-7-generic root=UUID=4c66da14-93b0-4d1c-85eb-dbaf1e28b836 ro single
initrd		/boot/initrd.img-2.6.27-7-generic

but I'm not sure if this is safe or not?
and how can I remove old kernels from the list .. I've already deleted old kerenels but they still show up in the menu

I've seen some


This is fine. yeah you probably did it right. 
To remove old lines from grub menu. Delete all sections except your first two in menu.lst

### Post by Trafferth on 2008-11-06
My move to Ubuntu 8.10 was from Ubuntu 8.04 on three machines (two desktops, one laptop).  In all three cases I performed a fresh install.  

The experience was much the same in all three cases: the older desktop (a C2D E4-series 1.8GHz, VIA mobo, 2GB RAM) needed the default gateway to be set manually, as usual (this has been an issue since Feisty), but the laptop (a Rock Pegasus 33) and the modern desktop (a C2D E8200 , Asus P5K, 2GB RAM) worked fine in this regard.  

An issue that has reappeared is that of getting digital sound out over SPDIF: in 8.04, sound worked out-of-the-box, but in 8.10 I have had to manually dig into the mixer to set the PCM volume (set to zero by default).  The laptop's sound worked just fine on Ubuntu 8.10.  However...

I also tried Kubuntu 8.10 on the laptop just to give KDE4 a whirl.  Bizarrely, the laptop's sound didn't work (although it works just fine on Ubuntu 8.10  In that case, in order to get it working, I had to use alsamixer, unmute the PCM and save the state with alsactl, in order to have (unmuted) sound work on boot-up.  I don't know if muted sound on startup is a widespread issue, but this fiddle solved it for me.

Apart from those niggles, I am very impressed with 8.10; it's clean, stable, and does what I want it to do (scientific computing, C++/Python development and LaTeX authoring, mainly) without complaint. :)

---

### Post by m.srivathsan on 2008-11-06
Yesterday night, I upgraded from Ubuntu Desktop 8.04 LTS (Hardy Heron) to 8.10 (Intrepid Ibex).

The Upgrade process, as expected, was smooth.  But after I rebooted into 8.10, I was disappointed :-(

1. Slower Graphics / Visual Effects

The Graphics (GNOME 2.24) was perceptibly slower than in 8.04.  I have Genuine Intel DG31PR Motherboard with onboard Graphics (no dedicated GPU), E6750 C2D CPU with Intel VT enabled, 2GB (800 Mhz) RAM, 250 GB SATA with 150GB occupied by WinXP.  Lastly, I have 64bit Ubuntu (right from 8.04).

I could really see the difference and could confirm it by booting with Kernel 2.6.24-21 which was there in 8.04.  The additional Visual effects of the GNOME Windows was enabled right from the time I installed 8.04.

2. "Ugly", Slow VLC

I understand that my VLC player was also upgraded in the process but I feel it is really ugly - with distastefully BIG buttons!  Also, the Movie playing is not upto the mark - in comparison with 8.04.  It is perceptibly jerky!

3. Strange behaviour with WinXP drives / Volumes

When I click - "Places" -> "User" (which is my D: in WinXP), I could only see an icon coming up on the Desktop whereas in 8.04, it also used to open the drive / Volume in a file explorer (or is it Nautilius?) window.  To add to my irritation, when I double-click the (mounted drive) icon on my Desktop, it also opens up the ugly VLC Player

4. Virtual Box and VMMPlayer not working any more

I had Virtual Box 2.0.4 and VMMPlayer 2.5 (to use the OpenSUSE + Mono 2.0 virt. appliance) in 8.04 and they were working fine.  Ofcourse I had to uninistall KVM before.  But now, I think KVM is again installed.  I didn't check further but probably these 2 work after I again remove KVM from Kernel 2.6.27 that comes with 8.10

SUMMARY
-------
I had been a RedHat / Fedora fan before.  6 months back, for the first time, I tried Ubuntu 8.04 Desktop after reading many favourable reviews about it.  And that was not a disappointment at all.  Infact I was so excited that I believed that I had a Linux distro that would help me completely replace Windows.  Even now, I believe that 8.04 Desktop is still worthy a competitor for Windows and is definitely better than 8.10.

In contrast to the euphoria I got after installing 8.04, 8.10 upgrade was a BIG DISAPPOINTMENT!  I have not tested it further but I hope that I don't have further disappointments with it.  But I should say that till now I have not got any "Show Stoppers".

But I have not lost hope.  I strongly believe that there would be another upgrade / patch that would rectify all the above points and I am looking forward for that.

Thanks and rgds,
Watson (from Bangalore, India)

Next, I had to figure out that I need to download an hsf modem driver, transfer it to the laptop (with a USB memory stick), install it (luckily I figured out I can just double-click that .deb file, phew!), and then need to configure and run something called wvdial or pon.  At least I knew all the ISP numbers and details there, but it took me a while to figure out the relationship between wvdial, pon (same thing really, just slightly different, isn't it?) and Gnome-PPP (a GUI sitting on top of wvdial, if I understood correct). ### Post by dcroxton on 2008-11-07

I haven't found any information on how to fix either, and none of my posts have been answered.  I might be able to live without two monitors (I didn't think it was that big a deal until I had to spend a few days without them), but I have to have my .Xmodmap because I use a lot of accented characters from various languages in my job.

This is very disappointing, obviously.  I saw someone suggest not to upgrade without first trying it in a virtual machine.  That might work on the .Xmodmap, but I don't think it will work for two simulated monitors.  I don't know, therefore, when it will be safe to upgrade.  I'm glad that the last version was LTS.

Re-installing Hardy was not that much trouble, and I have /home on a separate partition.  However, there are always packages that aren't in the repositories, and configuration files that aren't stored in /home or /etc:  Sun's VirtualBox (necessary for USB support), GCALDaemon, an up-to-date Festival, ies4linux, and others.  It's a big deal to have to go through this process.

### Post by jamouneau on 2008-11-07
My experience was mixed. Net upgrade through update manager was started and canceled due to impatience with slow net connection.

Torrent of livecd iso burned to disk. Clean install from livecd went great except that my network connection was unusable (this was disappointing but expected as the 8.04 install had the same problem).  The tweaks needed to get 8.04 working (my computer is a Lenovo Thinkpad T61p) had no impact on 8.10.

Changes needed to make 8.04 work:

added to /etc/sysctl
net.ipv4.tcp_sack = 0
net.ipv4.tcp_window_scaling = 0

changed/added to /etc/modprobe.d/aliases
alias net-pf-10 off
alias net-pf-10 off ipv6

Both wired and wireless network connections worked fine in 8.04 with these changes.

Re-installed 8.04 and got it networking again (changed as above). Decided to give update manager another try.  Net update process was slow! (Now know that you can use update manager from the livecd, check bottom of page [http://www.ubuntu.com/getubuntu/upgrading](http://www.ubuntu.com/getubuntu/upgrading)).

During update at the prompt "/etc/sysctl file is customized (or whatever), do you want to keep or replace this file?" Kept the file. Did not see a prompt on the aliases file (but the update kept the modified one).

Network connection under this way of upgrading to 8.10 is working fine and seems the same speed as with 8.04 ( don't have wireless setup so haven't checked that).

Real puzzling at how saving modified configuration files under an update works but making the same changes to the files from a fresh install fails.

Installed Nvidia driver and display seems quicker.

### Post by karhulitos on 2008-11-08
> **enofman said:**
> ...What I would like to know now is there a way to downgrade to Hardy? ...
Please HELP I do not want to go back to windows.
Gary

What I always before distribution upgrade (and every now and then w/o upgrade) do is
[LIST]
[*]take backup of whole disk with [PING]("http://ping.windowsdream.com/")
I have a 250GB disk on laptop and a cheap 250GB WD MyBook external USB disk. Around 100GB is used. Full image backup takes around 3-4h with gzip compression.
[*]try new version for a while
[*]restore back to previous or make a new backup of the upgraded version
Just did a restore back to Hardy and it took 1h 5min.
[/LIST]

So I don't offer you any solution now but perhaps for the future.
