### Post by whatthefu on 2008-11-08
I first tried to install Ubuntu 8.10 to replace Opensuse 11 because everytime I booted into OPensuse on my HP Pavillion dv9927cl. The problem I was having since upgrading to Opensuse 11 was evrytime the time selected for the computer to go to screensaver elapsed, the computer would freeze up giving cause to pull the battery to shutdown. Well, the problem must be a kernel or video driver issue, because the issue is still here. As long as I stay busy on the computer, it does not freeze up. I did not that when the computer freezes, my caps lock light flashes at about the same rate that my power button light and power indicator light flash when the computer hibernates in Windows. Maybe this is a clue and maybe it has something to do with the power save functionality.

The first time I tried to install Ubuntu 8.10, it installed, but would not launch the display server. So I tried it again and could not even finish the install. This I thought was odd since botting into the live CD work very well. I was even surprised to find out the my Wacom Bamboo table worked as well as in Windows Vista. (Well, I haven;t tried all of the functions yet.) So after I learned about the network upgrade option, I plugged in with an ethernet cable and actually got between 1.2 and 3.2 MBs download speed. My average was about 2.7. I had to install 8.04 before the upgrade, which went flawlessly.

Now when I boot into Ubuntu, I have to keep the key board busy to keep the boot process moving along. This is how it works. When the Ubuntu spalsh screen comes up during boot, the first progress bar that appears is one that has the progress graphic move right then back left. If I do not keep the space bar depressed, it will not move. Tonight when I booted into Ubuntu, I thought I would see how long it would take if I did not depress the space bar. After 5 minutes, I depressed the space bar and the bott process proceeded. After the first progress bar the next one changes the black bar to orange. This too took the occasional depression of the space bar to keep it progressing. I press the space bar when it stops progressing and it continues. During this phase of the boot up, Depressing the space bar does not always have immediate reaction. sometimes I have to let the computer do its thing for a few seconds or more before pressing the space bar has an effect. Tonight I became busy with something else for 23 minutes and when I press the space bar, the progress continued. Once it gets to the third progress bar changing the orange bart back to black, the boot process continues normally and I am presented with a login screen.

Compiz works fine after installing the propietary drivers using the hardware drivers menu selection under System-->Administration. I have done several uprades, but I figure the frezing thing is not an Ubuntu thing since it occurred while using Opensuse 11. The boot problem must be an Ubuntu thing since it did not occur with opensuse 11.

I have not noticed any other problems as of yet, but the two that I have are major. I think the one thing that would make Ubuntu the perfect distro, I mean beside fixing the two issue I am having, is to make a menu like that now used in Opensuse. It is a cool menu. Two clicks and I am there without guiding the pointer through a maze.

If it is any consulation, my Wacom Bamboo did not work in Opensuse. That is a BIG kudos to you Ubuntu guys. Thanks a bunch. I do seem to drink more coffee using Ubuntu than Opensuse though. It make me a might nervous when I drink it. Uggh.

### Post by Shazaam on 2008-11-09
Ran livecd first, amazed it would let me set the screen resolution up to 1600! WOW!
Performed a clean install on a pre setup partition (manual partitioning choice in installer) that went without a hitch. Re-booted pc and it went to 800x600 "Safe graphics mode". Fine, I will enable the restricted drivers. DISASTER! Black screen w/blinking cursor no matter what I did.
Ok, fine again. Installed envy. DISASTER! Same problem. You know that you are peeved when your head pounds in rhythm to the blinking cursor. So, giving up I went back to a tried and true method. Downloaded 177's from NVIDIA, did the kill X and gdm stop thing. Drivers popped right in, modules built, cool. Reboot. DISASTER! AUGGHHHHH!!!!!

Long story short, I found "xorg.confnew" sitting at / and the xorg.conf that was in the X11 folder was EXACTLY the same as the failsafe version. Copy/pasted/renamed the xorg.confnew to the /etc/X11 folder with a tweak or two and it now works fine. Beautimus.

Don't get me started on pulseaudio.

### Post by leandromartinez98 on 2008-11-09

1 - The webcam, which worked (after a lot of tinkering) in 
Hardy, does not work anymore, and it won't very soon, since
the driver is broken for the newer kernel (I'm very surprised,
since one of the claims of the new version was better
webcam support).

2 - The brightness control does not work anymore.

3 - The computer does not come back from sleep, need hard reboot.

4 - The system sound control (bips, etc), is very buggy, the sound
starts to work and stops working unpredictably.

5 - The computer crashed because the wifi switch was off and
the network was not found.

1) Audio in Skype did not work. Fixed by changing audio device in Skype settings to "pulse".

2) The key repeat rate on my bluetooth keyboard often gets stttttttttttttuck for a second causing the same character to be sent many times. This is not a physical thing -- the keys themselves are not getting stuck. I've tried adjusting all of the settings in System->Preferences->Keyboard but they have no effect.

3) After the machine has been on for a day or two, *all* sound stops working. The only way I have been able to get it back is by rebooting.

So #1 was relatively easy to resolve. #2 is a relatively minor annoyance. But #3 a major problem. Unfortunately searching for "sound problems" returns too many results, so I'm going to try to research pulseaudio (even though as a user I should not have to learn/care about my system's sound system). If I do not find anything, I am going to back-up my data, and do a fresh install after wiping the system disk. <sigh>

### Post by rclark68137 on 2008-11-09
The upgrade to Intrepid was smooth and pleasantly surprising.

At first, I freaked out after upgrading because wireless networking no longer worked. 

You see, I have a Linksys WUSB54G V4 using WPA2 and a hidden SSID. Ever since Dapper, I've had to jump through all sorts of hoops in order to get wireless to work. Stuff like uninstalling Network Manager, blacklisting the rt2500 driver, using the Windows driver with ndiswrapper, and editing my /etc/network/interfaces file. 

But imagine my surprise when I discovered that this hassle is no longer necessary. I can just use Network Manager and everything works!

I did have to uninstall ndiswrapper, remove the blacklisted entry for rt2500 in /etc/modprobe.d/blacklist, and remove all the wlan0 entries in /etc/network/interfaces.

This is a major improvement, and I'm extremely happy with Intrepid. Ubuntu keeps getting better and better!

### Post by Gingalone on 2008-11-10
After Upgrade the system didn't see internet, with hardware testing a networking error was detected, something about the default gateway...
Looking up in the Linux Infos Ocean on the Internet I got the solution (not in one minute but it was OK). I discovered the file /etc/network/interfaces apparently had lost the two lines about dhcp configuration:
auto eth0
iface eth0 inet dhcp
I put them back in the file and given the command: 
sudo /etc/init.d/networking restart
and the hardware testing said network OK and I become able to dive again in the Internet Ocean!
Now everything works perfectly with Intrepid Ibex!
Ciao everybody
Gingalone

### Post by cybergalvez on 2008-11-11
upgraded from 8.04 to 8.10 amd64.

I downloaded the alt disk and did the initial upgrade with that followed by an apt-get updage apt-get upgrade.

The upgrade went ok, but there have been problems that I have had to work through,
1) graphics, I have an nvidia 7600 video card and I was using the drivers from nvidia installed with envyng.  After the upgrade my graphics did not work properly until I reran envyng and installed the video drivers again.  note, I've done the upgrade twice now, once on my home computer and a second time on my work computer.  After doing this on my home computer when I upgraded my office computer, after the reboot I went right to the command line and did apt-get update, apt-get upgrade envyng -t before even trying to boot into X.
2) on my 64 bit machine (home) I had lots of trouble with packages being removed and not reinstalled.  For example I had k9copy installed, and after the upgrade I had to reinstall it along with all te kde libs. 
3) ia32libs did not initally install and would not install with the nvidia 173 driver installed, it wasn't until I installed the 177 driver that the ia32libs drivers installed properly.
4) I am finding other random libs that need to be reinstalled, I use bbclient to keep my dyndns url uptodate, and that needs a perl ssl lib which for some reason got killed during the update.  I did not find out until my IP changed and my computer was no longer available.  Found out by looking throught the sys logs and I saw the error message.

Suggestions to make it simpler in the future:

1) A report of all the packages that were removed and not replaced with newer ones should be made so that the user can update if needed.

2) During the install several configuration files were changed, and I had to decide during the installation what to do, I would rather that again the installation process make a list of config files that needed to be changes and then save the diff files for me to deal with later.  Or better yes simply save the original config files for me so that I could use a diff program later to resolve anything that may need resolving

### Post by darkstaar on 2008-11-11
What happened to Ubuntu?!?

I've been using *nix systems since I installed a long-since-forgotten version of Coherent on several 5 1/4" floppies onto my 16Mhz 386 back in 1991. I've been running Linux since Slackware 2.1. I've gone thru countless versions of both Red Hat and Mandrake/Mandriva and I've been running Ubuntu exclusively since 7.04.

With every new version of Linux that I've had the pleasure of using, I've been blown away at how much a particular distro has improved the Linux experience. This is especially true with the successive Ubuntu versions that I've used. Ubuntu's "it just works" slogan definitely applied here.

That was up until a week ago when I upgraded to 8.10.

Actually, the upgrade itself worked perfectly as I'd come to expect from Ubuntu, and it wasn't long before my laptop booted up into Intrepid.

Within an hour, it crashed. Completely. Right to the BSOD (Black Screen of Death). I've never experienced that before this with Ubuntu. And it did it again, and again, ad nauseum.

Then I discovered that Skype, which had previously worked pretty well out of the box since 7.04 was screwed under this new version. It took me several hours over two days to figure out the right combination of settings and drivers to enable the making a phone call, only to find out that I sounded like Alvin the chipmunk at the other end (seriously).

Another couple of hours of experimentation to fix that embarrassing issue, all the while dealing with these random crashes, and I'm beginning to figure out why they named this OS after my old '98 Dodge Intrepid.

They should've called it Ubuntu Vista.

Why did I have to spend sooooo much time fixing something that was never broken *before* this "New and Improved" version?

Next, I noticed that Flash videos no longer worked particularly well (YouTube and others). Amazingly, I'm able to watch as the final frame of the video flashes incessantly thoughout its entire length. Okay. I just figured that this was a minor bug that would be fixed soon.

A week into the upgrade and I noticed that the random crashing has suddenly stopped, no doubt due to one of the many bug fixes that have come in. Good.

But today, I found out that any application that uses OpenGL doesn't work at all anymore. I can no longer view earth in Google Earth (the program runs fine otherwise but what's the point?). In fact anything that utilizes OpenGL operates similarly. And Open Arena just isn't particularly enjoyable without video. This stuff worked just fine under all of my previous versions of Ubuntu but once again, we have a case of Ubuntu Vista 'fixing' things that were never broken.

These aren't the only issues I've been having with this version. I could go on but this post is getting lengthy.

So now, I've made my decision to get out of Intrepid. I just have to decide whether I'm going to downgrade (upgrade?) back to Hardy or switch to Fedora. But I know that I can't stay with this thing much longer. Every day with Ubuntu Vista brings more unpleasant surprises.

Just like my old Dodge Intrepid.

--Leisa

### Post by jimbudler on 2008-11-12
Three upgrades:

1. IBM desktop with Xeon Dual Core 3GHz, Nvidia NV37 Quatro graphics card and SATA hard drive.
Upgrade went fine until reboot, couldn't find hard drive. It could boot from the 8.04 kernel. Added rootdelay=60 to kopt_2_6_27 after experimentation and Googling.

2. Whitebox with Intel motherboard, 1 GHz Pentium III and ATI Radeon 9550 graphics card. Random freezes. Downloaded ISO and did an install instead of an upgrade. Disabled compiz. Seems stable now. Fortunately, I can do this easily since all my data, etc. is on a second hard drive. I can wipe the OS drive at will.

3. VM under VirtualBox on a MacBookPro. No problems, except incapable of running compiz. That isn't a surprise.

### Post by alibro on 2008-11-12
I upgraded from 8.04 to 8.10 last week. Mostly it went ok but had a few problems. 
Firstly during the upgrade I was asked what to do with the menu.lst. In my past experience when the menu.lst is changed during an upgrade my XP option is removed (I dual boot), so I chose to keep my existing menu.lst. BIG mistake, what the upgrade failed to mention is that by not letting it make the change I was not using the new Kernal. Hey that might seem obvious to some of you but I bet there are more people out there who wouldn't realise it. The upgrade continued and eventually rebooted the PC. Now my nvidia driver stopped working, I kinda expected that as I had the same problem with 7.10 last year so I tried to sort it out. After several hours messing about I eventually got stuck with a blank screen. 
Now the issue with not updating the menu.lst really showed itself. The Recovery mode option would not work as the relevant file was not there. After searching this forum I found how to fix it from a live CD and realised I hadn't been using the new kernal at all. 
Back to the Nvidia problems, after the initial upgrade I found it strange that even with all Nvidia drivers removed and a default xorg.conf, the restricted driver icon would not show to allow me to install the Nvidia driver. Now I was using the correct Kernal it came up just a few minutes after rebooting, and 5 minutes later both my screens were working fine. 
With hindsight I should have allowed the upgrade to make the changes but when you are being bombarded by questions and the consequences are not explained it is hard to know what is the right thing to do.

Hope this helps somone else
Alibro

Upgrade from Hardy 8.04 to Intrepid Ibex. I was Running Ubuntu 8.04 in English based in Germany, hence I had my Server Source set to Germany. I also had 3rd party repositories pointing to Akirad for Cinerella and to the Mplayer SMPlayer repository.

My Hardware is a Siemens-Fujitsu XI-2550

Upon starting the update, I was informed that the 3rd Party repositories were deactivated, the number of files to download was given as 1286. These were downloaded and then the upgrade hung up. The download manager Icon in the status bar upper right showed 680 new updates. Upon closing the update window I got a cryptic message that only a partial update can be accomplished owing to a failed update.

After some trial and error I found out that the German Server was missing some files, I then switched to the US main server and restarted the upgrade. 1288 Files were loaded and the upgrade completed successfully. During the upgrade I was asked several times if i wished to retain user defined configurations for xsane, Hewlett-Packard Printers, X-Windows, I decided to retain my configurations.

After the Upgrade (after the reboot and new login) I discovered the following:

Cinerella, Mplayer, SMPlayer had been deleted - I re-established the 3rd party repositries and reinstalled.

The Catalyst Controll Center for the proprietry ATI Radeon Driver had been deleted - I reinstalled.

Grip does not eject the CD after ripping and encoding despite this option being activated.

The overall Sound output level is very low (very quiet) I have tried all sound settings to no avail. Despite maximum volume, the sound output from all programmes Grip, Mplayer, Smplayer, VLC are hardly audible. I have a Realtek High Definition Sound Card. Changing the volume using the Hard Keys on the laptop (Fn Vol Up, Fn Vol down) display a loud speaker box and bargraph, this remains and the system hangs up. I have to switch off the computer and restart. Using the Loudspeaker Icon in the status bar works without hanging the system up. The touch volume slider on the laptop no longer works, worked with Hardy.

The Passkey for my W-Lan had to be reentered in order to establish a connection.

Shutdown is very sticky - Shutdown takes an awfull lot longer than Hardy did.

I have now have 2 Days experience with Intrepid, so I still have a lot of programmes and functions to tryout.

---

### Post by Therion on 2008-11-12
So when I do a little number crunching I come up with the following extrapolations:

~18% of over 1100 people report a "flawless" install.  That's fewer than 1 in 5 reporting an install without any issues.

~48% of over 1100 people report "many problems" with their install.  Statistically speaking that's half  or, to put it another way, roughly every other install reporting multiple issues.

---

### Post by togo59 on 2008-11-12
> **Therion said:**
> So when I do a little number crunching I come up with the following extrapolations:

~18% of over 1100 people report a "flawless" install.  That's fewer than 1 in 5 reporting an install without any issues.

~48% of over 1100 people report "many problems" with their install.  Statistically speaking that's half  or, to put it another way, roughly every other install reporting multiple issues.

I know there have been horrendous problems with graphics cards and the like but some problems, like the one I faced, turn out to be trivial, yet they are enough to stop or screw up an upgrade. But when they're fixed, we can't go back and re-vote. Also people will tend to be hovering around the "Installations" forum if and only if they have a problem. So, whilst accepting that there have been some huge issues, it's easy to under-estimate the number of seamless, problem-free upgrades.

If you ever upgraded from Windows SE to XP -- what a nightmare! None of the drivers worked and that was just the start!

### Post by cdtech on 2008-11-12
> **Spinx said:**
> I needed to hold down the enter key to advance the reboot.

You can add the "hpet=disable" to the kernel line within your /boot/grub/menu.lst. This should fix the "key to boot" issue.

---

### Post by AlanInVancouverBC on 2008-11-12
Mostly it's the internet access. The forums led me to this temporary solution:
In terminal, 
sudo ifconfig eth0 "my IP address"
and
sudo dhclient eth0

But I have to do that every time I boot Ubuntu--every time. When that's fixed, I'll be satisfied. Until then, I complain that I should revert to 10.04.

### Post by togo59 on 2008-11-13
> **Neobuntu said:**
> Let me see if I have this correct. ~82.04% did not go flawlessly. Why do you think that is? All we need now is more guys, crying how theirs (~17.96 %) went fine and so, "there is no problem".

Excuse me if I sound smug. If you can get people to recognize our open software option, at all, how is this helping non-technical people (about 75% of the population) get off of closed software(and farther reduce non-free driver problems)? You know, you can tell them to stay with 8.04 Hardy all you want to but they will try 8.10 Intrepid anyway.

Houston, we have a problem....

I write this knowing we will fix it and I will be a part of it.

Do you think better quality control is needed?

I may be over-egging this but since open-source developers do not have the massive resources of Micro$oft, they (presumably) rely on the community (you and me) to test all the permutations and combinations of drivers and sound/graphics/comms/motherboards etc.

Maybe too few of us downloaded the beta. Maybe too many waited for others to get their fingers burnt. It's easy with hindsight to say they should have tested this and that (and, with hindsight, they certainly should) but to all those who admonish us against downloading bleeding edge versions perhaps the current problems could have been foreseen if we had. E.g. I could have dual-booted 8.10 beta and 8.04 just to have a play but I waited until after 8.10 was released.

Why did I upgrade? Because it was there; I knew there were risks but so what? I didn't want to be left out. I think most lay users like me will think like that.

So maybe developers should encourage us to try the next beta version. Here's how: The beta should anticipate taking up a small amount of disk space and be dual booted with the previous version (or within the previous version as an application), with an easy uninstall. Alternatively provide an OS download sufficient just to test the peripherals, i.e. a lite-weight version just to test those permutations of drivers etc. Provided we weren't at risk, many of us would happily run tests and provide feedback -- it's the least we could do.

Forgive me if this already happens.:oops:

Just musing. I know nuffink really.

---

### Post by GoLinux on 2008-11-13
First time Ubuntu user, although I have been using other distros for over three years now.

My setup:

- IBM Thinkpad T41
- Running 8.10 off a 8Gb Sandisk Flash Drive

Issues:
- No sound in Skype, fixed fiddling with the Mixed Applet and Skype "Sound In", "Sound Out" and "Ringing" options
- Very slow boot (about 5 minutes!), but after that the system is fairly responsive. Definitely faster than running off the LiveCD, but I do not know how it compares with a full HDD installation. It does NOT feel sluggish at all, though.
- After a couple of updates through Synaptic I get a message error about not being able to update Linux-generic "something" (sorry I'm at a different computer now, can't remember the name of the module). Aparently it doesn't affect proper working of the system and I found a reference to it as a bug report on the launchpad web site.
- My old Intel USB webcam doesn't work (yet...)

Other than that, EVERYTHING works, including Wi-Fi, video/audio playing and streaming (after download of w32codecs and ubuntu-restricted-extras). I must say I'm impressed.

### Post by taygan on 2008-11-13
Oh yeah!  Upgrade went great!  I have a Gateway 1625, with the Realtek 8189 USB wireless (rtl8187b driver) and was using the patched driver mentioned here:
```
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WifiDocs/Device/RealtekRTL8187b](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WifiDocs/Device/RealtekRTL8187b)
```
I was a bit nervous on upgrade as those docs say it caused a crash, BUT I went ahead anyway, especially since the patched driver was shaky and didn't support encryption very well.

I backed up my data, uninstalled programs I didn't use, removed third party repositories, downloaded the alternate install amd64 iso so I could reinstall without downloading everything again (slow connection).

I booted into 8.04, popped in the alternate-install-amd64 cd, said yes to everything, downloaded an additional 440MB data overnight and woke up to a working 8.10!

THE WIRELESS WORKS GREAT!

I did have to: ```
sudo modprobe rtl8187b
``` to get the wireless up, and under 8.04 I wasn't autoloading the patch on boot, but rather had it as a desktop script for when I needed wireless.  I would suggest you remove it from your boot scripts when you upgrade.

Not only did I need the new kernel for the wireless, but also my Motorola ROKR wouldn't connect with 8.04.  With the upgrade to 8.10 I can load music and pictures no problem.

As for functionality, if 8.04 works for you, there's probably no need to upgrade.  But, for those with hardware issues, 8.10 adds significantly more support.

THANKS UBUNTU!

---

### Post by DataMatrix on 2008-11-14
Installation type: Upgrade from Hardy Heron 8.04

Notes:
-alsa isn't working, I've tried all possible fixes and then compiled OSS, now sound works (oss support by the gnome-mixer is better now :) )
-webcam is mirrored vertically
-display doesn't react to backlight changes, but atleast the system doesn't hangup.

### Post by GoldNugget on 2008-11-16

My experience with Intrepid is 2:2 right now.

### Post by balaknair on 2008-11-16

### Post by dummzeuch on 2008-11-16
Hi,

I upgraded from Kubuntu 8.04 to 8.10 and immediately was shocked how the usability had decreased with some new KDE features that seemed mostly to be taken (stolen?) from Windows Vista. That was one problem taken care of, even though I used to prefer KDE over Gnome, but definitely not anymore.

Another problem was my ATI based graphics card in conjunction with my SyncMaster 204B monitor. I had just solved a problem with Hardy where the monitor flickered when using a resolution over 1280x1024. The problem immediately came back with Intrepid. I have since been able to solve it again with switching to the new release of the proprietary ATI driver and modifying a modeline entry in xorg.conf (see [this post]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6183721&postcount=2")).

Then, there was yet again the problem of getting my printer to work. I had this before I switched to Ubuntu (Debian, SuSE, Mandrake) but this was the first time it happened with Ubuntu. The printer is an HP Laserjet 6P attached to the parallel port. Getting it to work again was a matter of several hours, since I was not familiar with the tools used in Gnome (I might have caused it myself by removing too many KDE related packages).

So, I definitely wouldn't call that a smooth upgrade. Add to that that the upgrade on my eee pc failed miserably (which is maybe worth a separate post), I was rather pissed off after I had spend most of a weekend to get a perfectly working system to work again after (unnecessarily) upgrading from 8.04 to 8.10. ### Post by apocalypso on 2008-11-16
My experience wasn't worry-free.

I upgraded from 8.04 to 8.10 and tried to do it at first using the upgrade manager, but then didn't like the idea of having to download well over 1Gb of data as the upgrade manager suggested. I then resorted to download the alternate cd and proceeded with it. Having done that, I realized I should have gone with the upgrade manager anyway since the fresh upgrade still had well over 500Mb of additional data to download... :confused:

In the middle of all this, my Nvidia 6600Le wasn't working right, I had to boot in safe graphics mode, and I was hoping this last batch of upgrades would solve it. Downloading these 500+Mb took me well over 4 hours and didn't solve the problem.

I looked here and there and everywhere and finally found out that it was a problem between the Nvidia driver and the kernel: my newly upgraded Ubuntu 8.10 was still loading the previous kernel (2.6.24-19) because, for some reason, the menu.lst file didn't updated itself to include 2.6.27-7. All I had to do was edit menu.lst and include the new kernel. Now my Nvidia driver is happy and all is seemingly back to normal...

I'll take extra cautions for my next upgrade.

---

### Post by Neobuntu on 2008-11-16
Nobody likes forced change. At least at first. With some benefits and techniques it is needed. Sometimes it is not.

I couldn't give a rats "hide end" about whether Vista or OS-X has a feature or which was first, I want the best anyway. Trying to be too different is a very limiting endeavour. We have enough to do, toward common usability, time saving and overall user friendliness.

I don't mean to sound ungrateful but lets, get 'er done! LOL

I have warmed to the unique KDE4 way. Some. After usage, I can see some reasons for some interface changes. 

Yet, I'm even more shocked at the not ready for prime time; overall state of 8.10 (Kubuntu). I think that if we assume the next release following an LTS version will stink, due to innovation, then it will. We need a new goal. Newbies **that know** about open software, simply say, "Linux" is broken. No matter what we say.

I propose the next releases that follows a LTS version, be more heavily started (and promoted) in parallel to the LTS version. This would encourage and allow more testing; by more testers. It also will not be called a release; until it's hopefully ready. This will hopefully be much more ready, at the Six month, known goal. This way, it can be cutting edge after Six months and also much more stable (ready for newbies). In fact, if we don't do something like this, Windows will rebound first. Not good.

---

### Post by silkstone on 2008-11-16
Please, please. please.... (how many more pleas do you need?)...

Stop this absurd reinvention of the wheel every six months. Focus on the LTS releases and keep them up to date - Flash 10, OOo 3.0, GIMP 2.6 for Hardy. All of these run perfectly on 8.04, but are not available from the standard repos.

Leave the intermediate releases for Bleeding Edge fans. Replacing the OS every three years is quite often enough for those of us who want to use Ubuntu as a stable, reliable OS. How long has XP been around?

The current upgrade/update policy is suicidal and totally unnecessary. I'm running 8.04 on four machines and wouldn't dream of 'upgrading' to something with as many bugs as 8.10 and with only 18 months support. But I'm stuck with outdated versions of bundled software.

For heaven's sake sort this out so there is always a stable release with up-to-date applications, and stop wasting everyone's time with a new release which may perhaps mostly work by the time it is superseded.

### Post by frodon on 2008-11-17
You are willing the stability of LTS and latest software, it's not compatible.

Nothing is preventing you from doing local install of softwares, it may make your next ubuntu version upgrate harder though.

The only place where new apps version can hit official ubuntu repo is in the backport repository otherwise you will have to use third party repositories or website like getdeb which provide up to date debs although the quality of the debs is sometimes lower.

I have 2 computers, on my laptop i want stability therefore i accept having less up to date softwares and only use LTS on it. This is not preventing me from keeping some apps like wine up to date through external repo.

[http://techlogbook.wordpress.com/2008/11/18/enable-wireless-connection-in-kubuntu-intrepid-810/]("http://techlogbook.wordpress.com/2008/11/18/enable-wireless-connection-in-kubuntu-intrepid-810/")

the other annoyance is that g77 is no longer in repository. Luckily I didn't upgrade my office desktop. I need to use g77 in my work. 
[http://techlogbook.wordpress.com/2008/11/17/installing-g77-in-ubuntukubuntu-intrepid-810/]("http://techlogbook.wordpress.com/2008/11/17/installing-g77-in-ubuntukubuntu-intrepid-810/")

I still haven't found easy ways to disable touchpad. But there is a way to solve this.
[http://techlogbook.wordpress.com/2008/11/07/disable-touchpad-in-kubuntu-810-intrepid/]("http://techlogbook.wordpress.com/2008/11/07/disable-touchpad-in-kubuntu-810-intrepid/")

### Post by captain.kipper on 2008-11-20
Had a problem with the nvidia drivers and apt-get. I have an old TNT nvidia card, and was using nvidia-glx-legacy driver. On upgrade to Intrepid Ibex it required me to change to the open source "nv" driver. This works fine (apart from some teething troubles at the start).

After upgrading, Apt-get (and the GUI update manager) kept failing to remove the old nvidia-glx-legacy - which means you can't install any software or update anything.
$sudo apt-get upgrade 
gives:
Removing nvidia-glx-legacy ...
dpkg-divert: error checking `/usr/X11R6/lib/modules/extensions/libglx.a': No such file or directory
dpkg: error processing nvidia-glx-legacy (--remove):
 subprocess post-removal script returned error exit status 2
Errors were encountered while processing:
 nvidia-glx-legacy
E: Sub-process /usr/bin/dpkg returned an error code (1)

Because packages are removed before new installs are made, this meant apt-get always failed to install/update other, unrelated packages. 

FIXED:
After looking on Launchpad I found a workaround:
$sudo gedit  /var/lib/dpkg/info/nvidia-glx-legacy.postrm 
and comment out (add # to start of line) the lines to do with the missing file (see error message). save and exit, the rerun apt-get. Bingo.

I hope this helps someone out there...
:)

### Post by odyssey41 on 2008-11-20
Made a clean install (secondary partition). Installation was flawless. Running well until all of the sudden system partially froze. Had to restart, after which system worked well again. This happened constantly. I was able to use my system for awhile with no problem until I did something, anything, like increase or decrease screen brightness (through the keyboard) or opened another window... only to find out that the system partially froze again. This happened many times... with desktop effects enabled, and without the desktop effects. I did not know what was going on. Call it "accident," but I think I found out the problem is related to the Power Manager. On one occasion it froze, I killed the Power Manager via the System Monitor and that was it... everything returned to normal. Anytime this happens, I kill the Power Manager and system works normally again. 

Anybody has experienced this problem? (Dell Inspiron 9300... Ubuntu 8.10... Nvidia 6800).

### Post by wburden on 2008-11-20

### Post by Guilden_NL on 2008-11-21
An update to my previous post about three excellent upgrades/new installs with one problem Acer laptop.  

After several hours of troubleshooting the startup options, I ended up with this working combination in my menu.lst "quiet splash irqpoll noapic acpi=off "

I upgraded from Hardy and kept copies of a few critical files, and menu.lst was one.  So after messing around with the start up without thinking of looking at the original (still slapping my forehead) I hit upon this combination.  The only difference was the need to add irqpoll.  I am not going to spend another minute trying to figure out what changed from Hardy to Intrepid to require this, just will post here with some key words in the hope that it will help someone.

Again, if someone with an Aspire is reading this, make sure that you uninstall Network Manager and install WiCD instead for wireless.  It works flawlessly upon install.

### Post by luceerose on 2008-11-22
> **larsenguitars said:**
> 
4) Youtube failure. Might not be upgrade related.


Sorry to quote myself but, I just found out...This is an Intrepid upgrade issue but seemingly only on 64-bit.
I've probably forgotten to mention that all of my Linux machines are 64-bit platforms. I'll have to add that to the specs in my signature.

Also, another problem just popped up. My printer (connected to the machine I just upgraded) won't network print from any other computer. I must just have to tell it to share the printer again.

EDIT: Can now print from my Main computer. Had to go to PrinterConfiguration >>> ServerSettings and tick 'Publish shared Printers connected to this system'.
Windows computer is the only computer left in the network I can't print from seems to be a firewall/port issue. I think I like that. I have to make sure that everybody can print from the Windows computer before Monday, but I have to admit, I always like security protocols that don't allow a windows system in.

EDIT 2: Installed Firestarter & allowed access to printers port designation. Printer problem solved.
Also fixed Firefox flash issue. Solution in Post#4 >>> [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=969826](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=969826)

Now the only issue left is the sporadically grey titlebar, but I don't really care about that.
All functional issues [SOLVED].
I stayed up all nite & it's now almost 7 in the morning. No sleep. But no more issues either.
It's a good thing it's a Sunday. I'm buggered.

Overall, not a bad install. But I would have to say they should probably test for a couple more weeks before release.

---

### Post by PorcelainMouse on 2008-11-22
This thread really had me worried.  So much so that I installed 8.04.1 Hardy Heron (Xubuntu) w/ LVM and full disk encryption on another system, updated it, installed a third party repository, and then tried the GUI upgrade button in Update Manger.

**No problems**.  During the upgrade process, it reported that it would remove 47 packages, including some linux-ubuntu-modules and linux-generic packages and one xorg-server package, which others seem to think was a bad sign.  It also safely disabled my thrid-party repository.  But, I didn't have any problems.  (Although, the volume adjustment in the tray disappeared on a *subsequent* reboot, which was weird, but very easy to fix.)

Now, my main system is x86_64 and I know I have some issues on that system which I suspect are related to architecture, so that upgrade might be different.  I can't afford to try right now, but I suspect these reported problems are not systemic and probably no worse than previous live upgrades.  I'll post on that upgrade too, when I do it.  I used the GUI upgrade to go from 7 (Gusty) to 8 and had several things change on me (like xorg/xrandr stuff), but nothing really failed.  Xubuntu is still my favorite distro, to date.

Best of luck to everybody!

### Post by jrt_ms1995 on 2008-11-22
I had no trouble installing or booting Ubuntu 8.10 this morning. My system is a Compaq SR5610f w/3GB, a 320 GB SATA hard drive, PNY PCI-e graphics card, and more-or-less generic Rosewill PCI wireless card, running Vista Home Premium. To the system I've also added an old 2.5" IDE HD to use in experimenting with Linux. I had been playing around with Linux Mint Elyssa, but after initially working flawlessly it suddenly could no longer connect to my wireless network.

Anyway, installed Ibex on the 2.5" drive, overwriting Mint, and the install went fine. The BIOS is set to boot first from this 2.5" HD, and GRUB is there. After removing the LiveCD and rebooting, Ubuntu started up quickly, with no troubles, and I readily connected to my network. Trouble came when I later tried to boot up Vista. No luck, either with normal boot or recovery boot, both failed with errors (21 and 13, respectively, if I remember correctly.) This problem has been discussed several times elsewhere in these forums, as I learned today, but none of the solutions presented worked for me.

I found my problem, however. Though booting was working fine with Mint and Vista, for some reason when Ubuntu reinstalled GRUB on my 2.5" disk, it wrote in menu.lst that Vista and Vista Recovery were at hd(0,0) and hd(0,2) respectively, when they're at hd(1,0) and hd(1,2). Edited menu.lst to reflect the right values and I'm back to Vista with no problems.

### Post by feydrutha on 2008-11-23
Somehow I have a feeling these polls are always biased towards failures... maybe just because people are more likely to check the forums when things break than when they just work.

Upgraded from hardy my Dell inspiron 1501 (with 32 bit ubuntu), and I now have everything working perfectly.

With the latest BIOS from dell, and ndiswrapper for wireless, everything works fine:

-wireless connecting even to WPA2-secured access points with no configuration file editing (with the proprietary driver instead of ndiswrapper, wireless worked only for un-secured APs). To get ndiswrapper working, you can follow [_this_]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WifiDocs/Driver/bcm43xx/Feisty_No-Fluff") guide (which was for feisty but it still works) if you have a broadcom wireless chip.

-suspend/resume working

-external monitors working (ati catalyst control center is now installed by default, so I should not need to do any xorg.conf editing. Haven't tried anything fancy yet though, just connected to a monitor and got a picture a the right resolution)

-pulse audio working (i recommend installing pulse audio volume control, which is just cool. You can individually control the volume of each application from a single volume control window)

Now I think I'll try the new encrypted Private directory thing with ecryptfs and move some of my stuff there (like emails, ssh keys, tracker index, skype logs,...)

### Post by Philio on 2008-11-23
The desktop install of Intrepid is most certainly the most unstable and annoying to date. I mainly use Ubuntu on servers and there is never any issue here thankfully.

The install 'should' be easy, it's quick and easy from a usability perspective however the new migration assistant is a big pile of crap and no option by default to disable it! Wasn't overly impressed about having to wait ages for it to copy 10's of Gb from Windows and then crashing half way through continuously. I found the switch to disable this on the installer (why is there not a tick box in the installer????) then to go all the way to the end and grub install failed. In the end I had to format my /boot partition in order to get the grub install to work correctly, which shouldn't have been necessary.

Despite the negativity towards the new migration assistant, it is a nice feature, BUT it's distinctly lacking in usability. Not everyone wants to import their Windows (or other Linux distro) settings, or all of them at least.

The desktop installer is slower and more problematic than any previous Ubuntu release. On the other hand the server upgrade runs like a charm and only took a minute or 2.

A few things that would be nice to see in 9.04 (desktop):

1. Allow users to enable/disable migration assistant from the GUI.
2. Allow users to selectively import information with the migration assistant.
3. The above in the form of a simple page that says 'Ubuntu can import your settings from your other operaterating systems, please select them from list' with an advanced button or something to configure exactly which settings are tranfered.
3. Improve crash handling so that there is an option to retry certain things or skip non-esential steps in order to complete the install and not have to start again from scratch.

### Post by stanley45 on 2008-11-23

I set aside an older desktop for a test machine, and tried to load 8.10, intending to dualboot with XP.  I never saw anything so weird.  It failed in the partitioning (repeatedly), so I gave up temporarily.  I tried partitioning with PartitionMagic, and - wow - Ubuntu seems to have created 7 copies of a SCSI drive.  Windows, when rebooted, had all eight copies listed in its Control/System/Hardware service.  I removed 7 but they came back when I rebooted.  PartitionMagic has no facility for removing drives, so I was stuck.  I have no idea how Windows or Ubuntu could think there were 8 identical copies of a drive.

I removed the SCSI drive, and tried installing again with just an IDE onboard. The partitioner inside 8.10 didn't see Windows, and only gave me an option of a whole drive for Ubuntu, or manual partitioning.  At least when I had the 8 copies of the SCSI drive the Ubuntu partitioner showed me the Windows used-space, and offered to work around it.

Now I am partitioning prior to loading Ubuntu 8.10 to see if this might work.  PartitionMagic recognizes the Window space.

I hope this is not an omen...

### Post by soccerush10 on 2008-11-24

**Pros (the stuff that works):**
[LIST]
[*]Update process was flawless (though understandably slow)
[*]WiFi works by default in Ibex, not in Hardy
[*]A list of recommended NVidia Video drivers (not available through Hardy)
[*]Faster, and just cooler in some undiscernable but notable regard.
[/LIST]
**Cons (the stuff that doesn't work, YET :wink: , and that never worked properly on Hardy)**
[LIST]
[*]Suspend and Hibernatet are non-functioning with the new video driver ( will get to this sooner than later, just like I did on Hardy)
[*]Fan needs to _speed up_ at higher temperatures otherwise CPU temp gets to 100 degrees C.
[*]and I STILL can't find the time between work and school to fix these things...but I look forward to doing it :)
[/LIST]
Awesome job so far, Ubuntu team!  Keep up the good work!

### Post by jstevans on 2008-11-25
I did a clean install onto a completely wiped HD - it was amazing!

I've been trying for weeks to get a small Linux distro running and booting on my beloved Sony 505 mini notebook by placing its HD into one of my desktop machines and configuring it there (the Sony cannot netboot and has no CD or floppy - both lost long ago) . I've tried half a dozen distros, many would not even boot in the desktop I'm using to host the laptop's drive (I get the black screen of death), others were painful to install to the HD or, even after all the annoyance, never could be convinced to boot properly from the HD. Xubuntu 8.10 booted, installed with incredible ease, automatically connected to the Internet via my home network, etc. It even found and installed my network printer perfectly!  

Absolutely amazing! Thanks to all who made this possible. If Linux is ever going to gain significant end-user market share this is a model of how to get there.

However, it's only 99% perfect. Well, maybe 98%. I had, and still have, some networking issues.

Initially I could not figure out how to make the Xubuntu machine visible to my Windows PCs. The Xubuntu instructions say I can change the host name by using "Applications &#8594; System &#8594; Network." But, there's no such command in Xubuntu 8.1.0. So, I started hunting for a likely candidate.

It turns out that "Applications &#8594; System &#8594; Shared Folders" produced an alert saying I needed to install Samba and NFS. So, I told it to go ahead and do so. I also used the "Shared Folders" GUI to rename the workgroup. Well, all that didn't enable my Windows machines to see the Xubuntu one or it to see the Windows machines. So, making a guess, I rebooted and now my Windows PCs can see the Xubuntu one - solid progress - yay.

However, I still cannot figure out how to see the Windows machines from the Xubuntu one.

The "File System" window does not even hint at there being machines out on my network. It does show (in the sidebar) the folder on the Xubuntu machine that I have shared and which can be seen by my Windows machines.

So, with that background, can anyone help me figure out how to see the Windows machines from my shiny new Xubuntu one?

Thanks.

### Post by lipinski on 2008-11-25
> **jstevans said:**
> 

The "File System" window does not even hint at there being machines out on my network. It does show (in the sidebar) the folder on the Xubuntu machine that I have shared and which can be seen by my Windows machines.

So, with that background, can anyone help me figure out how to see the Windows machines from my shiny new Xubuntu one?

Thanks.

jstevens - did you ensure that Sharing is enabled on your Windows machine?  A quick test is to right click on any folder (My Documents, for example), and Click Properties.  When the properties windows opens, you should see a Sharing tab.  If you do not see a Sharing tab, then sharing is not enabled on your Windows machine, and you won't see anything from your XUbuntu machine.

Enabling it depends on what version of Windows you are using, i.e., XP Home, XP Pro, Vista, etc.

Check out:
support.microsoft.com/kb/304040 

for help on how to enable the different types of sharing in Windows.

---

### Post by jstevans on 2008-11-25
In reply to the question "i am sorry but can someone tells me what does interpid Ibex mean?"

Each Ubuntu release has a name as well as a numerical designation.  In the case of release 8.10 the name is "Intrepid Ibex."  Why?  Who can know.  I find the numerical designations simpler to deal with but the community seems to like the names.

### Post by auryn29a on 2008-11-28
I started upgrading my Thinkpad R61 yesterday from 7.10 to 8.04, then from 8.04 to 8.10.  After many grueling hours of upgrading and scouring forums for answers to my problems, I now have a system that works except for 3d graphics.  I can't figure out how to compiz working again.


**Problems that I've managed to resolve:**
Keyboard went all wonky, arrow keys didn't work. I changed the keyboard layout to "evdev-managed" and it's fine now.
Scroll button on the trackpoint didn't work. Now it even works horizontally!
For a while I didn't have sound. I'm not sure how that got fixed.
Wireless. Always a headache on laptops.  It now works, but I can't get the bloody wireless led to stop blinking! It's driving me nuts! I finally put some tape over it.
Firefox went all dumb.  It didn't show my bookmarks or allow me to go back a page or anything.  Changing permissions on $HOME/.mozilla fixed that.


**Problem I'm still working on:**
3D graphics.

### Post by joker77 on 2008-11-30
First I upgraded from 8.04. Problems noted were(some of them started after a few days of updates)
1) hangs while shutting down. A bit inelegant but effective solution was that of P os ter 'Suzan' in the launc hpad bug report -  modifying the alsa-utils file. 
2)nm-applet was usually absent. didn't try any stunts for that one
3)the system would not respond appropriately when it was supposed to hibernate/halt/suspend on closing the laptop lid. 
Problems 1 and 2 were reported and discussed by others on the forum.

Then when updates over the last month did'nt fix the above problems, I tried the live CD. Everything seemed fine. So i did a fresh install. Things are working fine now except problem 3 above. (not a big problem- I'm not fussy) I'm afraid of recommended updates affecting shutdown and nm-applet so I've allowed only security updates, till I get some kind of green signal from this forum. 

One thing I noted after the fresh install was that quick-search on synaptic package manager was returning wrong results for key terms that you entered. You could scroll down the list and find it manually though. The search button seemed ok.

In summary: I had a much better experience with a fresh install.

### Post by TVTrukChik on 2008-11-30
I'm glad I didn't read this thread before I upgraded a couple of weeks ago.

Backed up what I needed, started the upgrade from Hardy through update manager, and went to bed (my internet connection isn't the fastest).  Responded to a couple of prompts in the morning, rebooted, and it's working fine, including Compiz, audio, wireless, and ATI proprietary drivers.  

Didn't have to reinstall any programs, although I'm pretty sure I told it to remove obsolete packages.  It didn't even change my wallpaper, which was mildly disappointing for some reason.

System is Intel dual core, Intel mobo, 4GB RAM, Radeon X1950Pro video, onboard audio, and Airlink101 wireless card (internal).  Intrepid also recognized my Trendnet USB wireless adapter that I got because Vista doesn't like the Airlink101 card.  The Trendnet adapter didn't work with Hardy.

I will say that I did have a little trouble figuring out Network Manager, just because it's different.  I was looking for the name of the wireless adapters (wanting to disable one of them) but all I could see was the name of the wireless network until I discovered that opening THAT up showed me the adapters.

Beginner's luck, possibly.  I've been using Linux for about 6 months.

One issue I noticed right away was the top of the windows don't seem to update properly.

I'm using Nvidia GeForce FX Ultra 5200 graphics card, running the Nvidia accelerated graphics driver (version 173), which is the recommended driver. I tried version 96 of the driver which seemed to "cure" the issue with the top of the window but just killed the menu text in OpenOffice.org.

### Post by kneewax on 2008-12-02
In the early days of this thread I posted saying that my upgrade from Hary to Intrepid was pretty seemless - a few issues but nothing significant.

However I thought I'd drop by to update y'all.

This afternoon I completed a roll back to Hardy.  Although none of the errors I had were fatal, I just couldn't face the constant battle I was having with Intrepid to keep it running.

My biggest gripe was the difference in resources needed to keep intrepid happy:  I run a two year old Fujitsu Siemens Amilo Pro v8010.  It has 1Gb Ram and a Centrino Mobile Processor rated at 2.05Ghz.  So although not super-beefy its a respectable machine.  

In Hardy this machine ran without major issue.  After upgrading to Intrepid it soon became apparent that there was a serious performance issue.  Simply tasks would cause the 'grey out' that meant the machine was struggling to find resources.  Running VirtualBox, always a seemless process in Hardy, became a real chore.  The sound system would flake out, if any other process was running and if I yried to run more than two applications at a time, the machine would slowly grind to a halt.  

Now some of these issues may be down to the upgrading needing a better machine, but it felt to me like RAM and other resources just arn't used as efficiently in Intrepid as they have in previous versions.   A host of other monor issues - small but annoying things like being unable to get gSynaptics to work under Intrepid, even with the fixes on this forum - have meant that for now I am stepping back and returning to Hardy.

For my machine at least Hardy is a much more stable release.

---

### Post by rnevins82 on 2008-12-03
Hi Guys (and other girls, lol)

### Post by henrik65 on 2008-12-05

### Post by russofris on 2008-12-05
Good afternoon,

Problems that I had with intrepid:

Using AMD64 Kubuntu:
1:  FB on boot worked sometimes, other times reverted to text, sometimes black screen, sometimes hard lock (Nvidia 8800GT)
2:  Shutdown halted system, but didn't actually shut down
3:  LiveCD rebooot message suggested that I eject the cd, but the tray was locked (Model=LITE-ON DVDRW LH-20A1L, FwRev=BL05)
4:  Rebooting from windows to Ubuntu would result in no video.  Cold restart required.
5:  Right click, share folder (utilizing samba/dolphin) did not work.
6:  Bluetooth did not work
7:  Stuttering audio when using the xine backend (Intel Corporation 82801I (ICH9 Family) HD Audio Controller).

Using stock x86-32 build.
1:  No bluetooth
2:  F-spot....  Gnome has a folder called "Pictures" in ~/...  F-spot creates/uses ~/Photos by default.
3:  None of the available audio players handle large (>50,000 songs) collections gracefully.  Currently using Exaile as it seems to work correctly, but slowly at times.
4:  Had to install mdadm and cryptsetup for my storage array.  These should probably be installed by default.

Overall, the x86 32 release isn't that bad (with the exception of bluetooth).  Don't touch kubuntu or the 64bit releases with a ten foot pole.

Thanx Muchly,
Frank

step 3

tell friend open a terminal like this (and dont get scared)

Applicatinos > Accesories > Terminal

then tell him to type

[COLOR="Black"]sudo apt-get install openssh-server[/COLOR]

and enter

then tell him to type
 sudo su

and tell him to watch for the # thingy

now  type

passwd

make a nice password

repeat said password and


now for u to ask the adress ( typing youripadress in a browser will do)

aaaaaaannnnnnnddddddd


ssh -X [email]root@(the.ip.you.got[/email])

your password AND YOU ARE IN

since you are root

type gparted and you can format the drive as if you were there

when done

type 

ubiquity

now is the installer

go install as you usually do and tell friend to do some zen in fron of the machine and phone you when the installation finishes (one hour maybe two)




go grab a munch watch some tv browse the web



then its easier to install apache mysql php or whatever

sudo apt-get upgrade
```

Nothing happened! Absolutely nothing. Yeah, the update ran OK, but when it came to the upgrade, nothing at all happened.



Weird

No not weird at all... 
sudo apt-get upgrade just updates your current install ....

you need to run
```
sudo apt-get [COLOR="Red"]dist-upgrade[/COLOR]
```

this will upgrade your current ( feisty / gutsy / ... ) to the current Intrepid

### Post by cygnus-X1 on 2008-12-24
](*,)](*,)](*,)  I downloaded it 3 or 4 days after the release date, like 8.04. Finally got around to loading it on a fresh SATA. Like 8.04, it *loaded* just fine. Added the needed and desired software. And when I started to actually *use* it... Crash, bam, boom.

First, Firefox was slo-o-ow. After a few days (yeah, days), system started hard locking with no error logs, like 8.04. (BTW - 8.04 also does random reboots as well. Which is real nifty when your right in the middle of doing something extremely important and/or with a deadline. #-o) Every time a hard lock occurred I'ld enter recovery mode to have it fix itself. Then reload the ATI driver. Reset Compiz. And go at it until the next hard lock. 

Today it totally crashed. It would not even enter recovery mode, failed on fdsk (or whatever it said), and since I'm a bit weak when it comes to CLI knowledge... I'm going to try 7.10 to see how it works. (I'm using it 'Live' right now to post this.) It's not like I'm running a P3 or anything. The machine I'm running has 2G memory (that checks out fine), and an AMD64 X2 4850e (dual 2500) CPU. 

I'm not trying to sound rude or the like. This is just my experience. I like what Ubuntu has to offer. Some of the available software is awesome, though I'ld like to see something that would allow me to run my Commnad and Conquer games on it! \\:D/ But stability problems really need to be addressed soon, as it is hardly professional, IMHO, to keep pressing forward without fixing significant problems. It's reminiscent of, dare I say, MS-XP onwards. And how can the MS stranglehold be broken with unreliable releases? 

I'll keep trying to get one of these Ubuntu releases to work, as I support their ideology. But sorry to say, I'm going to stick with my ratty old P4 with the dying Asus P4B533 running Win 2K as my mainstay. It's much more stable. Any _helpful_ info to fix these issues would be greatly welcomed via email. 

Peace to all and Happy Winter Solstice!  :guitar:

ADDENDUM: Problem Solved! After doing some heavy digging, I found out that the SuperTalent Memory I **_HAD_** in both mobos (Abit & Gigabyte) didn't live up to spec and couldn't handle the minimum voltage output. I changed over to the G.Skill 2x1GB and the problems went bye-bye. Now I've upped it to the G.Skill 2x2GB and things are going much smoother. Yippee!  :guitar:  Anyone interested in any cheap 2x1GB 1.8v SuperTalent memory?  :lolflag:

### Post by StudioDave on 2008-12-28
My new install of Ubuntu 8.10 has been a most trying experience, with a number of problems as yet unresolved. I re-iterate what I've posted elsewhere in the wilderness known as the Ubunutu Forums:

Machine: HP G60-125NR
CPU: AMD Turion-X2
RAM: 3GB
HD: 250 GB
OS: Ubuntu 8.10
video: nVidia 8200M
audio: Intel HDA

Shutdown/restart don't work properly. They either hang the machine entirely, or if I'm lucky I can ctrl-alt-del to reboot into recovery mode, from which point I can then issue a clean 'shutdown -h now'.

Logout from a terminal totally destabilizes the system and requires a hard reset. I think that this bug alone is enough to make me not recommend Ubuntu 8.10, and it's sad to think that it was not spotted before release. Byw, the offense seems to occur at the 'reloading system log' point.

For some reason HAL insisted on polling my empty SDM card slot and the DVD drive every two seconds, which eventually rendered the system unresponsive. I don't even want to know why this default exists, but it is a train-wreck until I disable HAL polling on those drives.

I'm also trying out Ingo Molnar's patched rt-kernel, which is likely to cause problems, but I don't think it's causing the shutdown/restart/logout troubles.

8.10 is a crapshoot for notebooks/laptops. Look at the results of this thread's poll: Fully twice as many people have reported that they have severe problems as have reported unqualified success with the system.

Btw, I'm using the i386 installation on a dual-core machine, thanks to a bug (hardware?) that prevents some 64-bit systems (Arch, Fedora) from installing (OpenSUSE 11 installed after some voodoo mojo). However, I need certain software that won't run on a 64-bit system, so that's no big deal.

Please don't tell me to read the previous posts regarding these problems. Trust me, I've read and re-read them until I can quote their content in my sleep. I've tried every suggested fix, to no avail, or worse. For example, adding the ifconfig fix for ALSA during shutdown/restart will completely hang the machine.

Perhaps NetworkManager needs some attention from the devs ?

Well, at least 'killall pulseaudio' works better than in OpenSUSE 11. :)

---

The weak give up and go back to paying exorbitant prices for their operating system and software while the more resilient stick it out on these boards trying to find out why the new "safe release" isn't working, usually to no avail.

The idea isn't so far-fetched, either. Warner Brothers, Disney, Sony (among many others) are using the same frustration tactics on the torrent community:
[http://torrentfreak.com/mpaa-caught-uploading-fake-torrents/](http://torrentfreak.com/mpaa-caught-uploading-fake-torrents/)

Just my .02

### Post by oceanexplorer on 2009-01-02
Well my Linux knowledge is growing quickly it has to be said!! 

However upon installing Ibex (I finally had enough of M$ Vista) and selecting to run the LiveCD it hung at the message "Checking battery state", at first I was stumped, then I tried alt + F2 and this got me to a command line, woohoo! So from there I tried startx and it seems that it cannot handle my graphics card, which is an ATI Radeon HD2400, nothing amazing. 

I was really disappointed that Ubuntu did not recognise my video card straight out of the box, however I was determined to resolve this and a after a few attempts I got it working by doing the following from the command line:-

(Well firstly plugged laptop into the router with a network cable so I could access the Ubuntu repos)

sudo apt-get install xorg-driver-fglrx jockey-gtk
sudo aticonfig --initial
startx

hope that helps

Paul

### Post by Hybrid-photog on 2009-01-03
A few years ago, I got a copy of Mandrake 9.0. It was tried out, but various bits didn't quite work as smooth as I'd have liked. However, I was determined to give it another go... but on the next version.

9.1 came out. It worked, 100%. Every bit of hardware I had was useable. My life in Linux had begun. I was introduced (forced?) to Vim, thanks to having to edit the crontab... to this day I still prefer Vim. And for when the desktop died/failed/vanished, there was "midnight commander" available. The Mandrake community wasn't anywhere near as hostile as the Redhat one. Replies of "RTFM" were few and far between.

However, dark clouds were forming on this peaceful and idylic setting. 9.2 wasn't as enjoyable as 9.1. Mandrake became Mandriva. Alterations to the naming sequence were done. Security updates became increasingly awkward to apply... editing of files had to be done for any updates to be installed. The head honcho of Mandrake was got rid of (iirc). Things were not alright.

Onwards, I persevered with Mandriva 2006. But it was becoming increasingly glitchy. Debian 5 was being finalised. Time to jump ship, methinks (methought?). I began to download VDIs and netinstallers of other Linux OS's.

Suse... no thanks. Redhat(e)... $DEITY no. Slack... no thanks. Gentoo... not yet. Debian 4... installer kept failing. Ubuntu... er... not as nasty as I thought.

Kubuntu 8.10 was researched and decided upon. Backups were done, to safeguard years of accumulated junk. Kubuntu was installed. Kubuntu wasn't bad, but KDE4 wasn't as smooth as I'd have hoped. And a couple of weeks later, the install decided to loose the wireless connection.

Lost in a version of Linux I was unfamiliar with, I realised that I hadn't dumped the Kubuntu disc image to a non-rewriteable disc... and that the only copy of Kubuntu had been written over with something else (Savage 2, I suspect). Using my other halfs PC, I got a copy of Ubuntu 8.10. It was installed.

The lessons I'd learned with Kubuntu stood me in good stead with Ubuntu. Plus, Gnome has really grown up since I last saw it (back in MDK9.1). And, what's more... the bluetooth dongle works fine in Gnome.

Hello all. :)

### Post by yther on 2009-01-22
Well, I want to add my two bits to this thread.

I have a Dell Inspiron 1520, and previously I had put Hardy on alongside the pre-installed Vista; it was a refurb so I didn't get to specify the OS.  Now Hardy mostly worked; it detected the extra multimedia buttons correctly and gave me usable video out of the box, but I could not use a secure wireless connection due to lack of drivers.  I didn't play with it much.

I had been using Gentoo on a Mac G4 and a couple of x86 boxes; I liked the feeling of control as I got to set everything up by hand, and it was nice to know that I could install just about anything in the world as long as it had a source tarball available, using a simple command and a small config file.  Gentoo is a wonderful example of the power of Linux, and if you want to customize it the sky is the limit!

However, the same aspect of setting things up by hand got old after a while.  It's great if you have weird hardware or feel the need to tweak everything, but now I would rather be doing other things for fun than configuring my system, and I am planning to build a new computer for my entertainment and other uses.  I would prefer something that "just works," while leaving me the ability to tweak it as needed.  Noticing that Intrepid was out, I decided to blow away Hardy and check it out.  I burned a CD of the 64-bit Kubuntu version and set to work.

Installing was straightforward.  I formatted /, chose my mount points for /home and the other volumes I still had from before, set up my locale and sat back.  When it was done, I restarted and found myself in the bizarre, empty world of KDE4.1, which I had expected.  The first thing I did was test my wireless, which now works just fine for either public or private networks.  Fooling around a little more, I loaded some extra packages and was able to bumble about on the Web, play a DVD, download torrents, view Flash content, play music files, edit text documents and spreadsheets, and run virtual machines.  Right there is 90% of what I use a computer for on a daily basis.

Further testing random things, I popped an SD card into a slot on my laptop; it was recognized and I could browse it.  Plugging in the USB cable from my Olympus camera, however, gave me no results.  After a brief struggle, I managed to convince the system to keep my volume at an audible level even after I reboot.  Next I will try making GRUB a bit prettier.  ;)

So, all in all, a much better experience than I had with Hardy.  A few inconveniences remain, such as slow graphics (waiting for the 180.whatever NVIDIA driver to find its way into EnvyNG) and the inability to browse my camera, KDE apps that crash for no good reason, and the constant spinning down of my hard drive when I don't have any torrents running.  I'm sure all of these will be overcome in time.

Never before have I had such a smooth experience installing Linux on a laptop!  (Ask me about the "fun" of installing Gentoo on a Compaq laptop with a 40GB hard drive and interchangeable CD/floppy drive...)  After all these years, we've come a long way.  :KS

When I get my new system built in the next couple of weeks, KDE-flavored Ubuntu will be the first OS I install on it.  If it doesn't work, Gentoo will be the second.  ;)  Windows will remain confined to virtual machines.

### Post by Wolf-Ekkehard on 2009-01-24
I posted my upgrade experience earlier right after I upgraded, but I spoke too soon!

I happen to use Axiom quite frequently; but it is completely broken - just doesn't work under Intrepid! This is a known issue, as I found out later.  I resist the temptation to comment on Ubuntu releasing a broken app...

Moreover, when I tried to re-install my printers (caused by a bug in system-config-printer-kde) all of CUPS got ruined - couldn't get it to work anymore since.  No help from the forum either :(

Lastly, KDE4 is disappointing! IMHO it is the Vista of Linux: lots of useless eye-candy (isn't it great that you can rotate your yellow post-it at arbitrary degrees on the screen??), bugs in crucial places (system-config-printer-kde, task bar not hiding...), and a lot of User Experience changes for the sake of change with no obvious benefit (lots of functionality gone from "System Settings" that now needs to be hunted down elsewhere)!!

Too bad I can't vote anymore, now that I have more insight.

My recommendation: 

[LIST=1]
[*]If you need Axiom, under no circumstances upgrade to Intrepid.  This is serious!!  

[*]If you might get tempted to reconfigure your printers using KDE4 tools, don't!!  They are broken.  Only use the CUPS WEB-based tool.
[/LIST]

### Post by Sunflower1970 on 2009-02-01
Fresh install if Intrepid last night on my Laptop. Ran into a few minor problems... Laptop has the 7500 Mobility Radeon in it. Under Hardy the Compiz effects worked very smoothly, but this time they were very slow, and choppy. Did a search on the forum, found this post: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1051571&highlight=ati+radeon+driver](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1051571&highlight=ati+radeon+driver) and got it to work beautifully.

My other snag is being able to come back out of suspend and have wireless work. It did in Hardy, but doesn't now. Did another search and it seems to be a regression somewhere in the kernel from Hardy to Intrepid (I had the same problem in Gutsy). 

A major happy surprise was that Network Manager worked flawlessly. Something it hasn't ever done before for me. It even worked while in the live CD version (again, it hasn't worked that well in the past for me). :)

But other than those two problems, Intrepid seems to be a lot faster on this laptop  than Hardy, which was something I wasn't expecting..

All in all I'm very pleased :)

ETA: After 24 hrs, I think I've found a fix for my suspend/wireless problem from this:[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/IntrepidReleaseNotes#Wireless%20doesn%27t%20work%20after%20suspend%20with%20ath_pci%20driver](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/IntrepidReleaseNotes#Wireless%20doesn%27t%20work%20after%20suspend%20with%20ath_pci%20driver)

I :heart: these forums :D

### Post by solwic on 2009-02-01
> **jsearles said:**
> If these problems are not resolved by tomorrow evening, this will be my last foray into the evil world of Linux.

Don't tell us.  Ultimatums don't work here.  If you don't like Linux, don't use it.  Doesn't bother us any.  We're glad you tried it, and hope you'll give it another go in the future.  

If you want it to work, make it work.  Otherwise, use whatever worked before.  Obviously there was a reason you tried Ubuntu though, so why not push through rather than letting the anger get to you and drive you away?  

> **jsearles said:**
> 
Seems that since NVidia was approved for sales on the Microsoft XBox360, they have conveniently forgotten that they have Linux users. I would too. After all they are a business.

I recently bought an nVidia 8400GS that I've had no trouble with, other than Ubuntu refusing to notify me of a newer driver.  But the driver was in the repos, so a quick update to the 180 driver and voila, issues solved. 

Besides, ATI's new driver supposedly (heavy emphasis on that word) has fixed the composite rendering issues, and video cards are cheap, even for good ones.  My 8400GS has 64 bit GPU and RAM, with 512MB memory and a PCI-E x16 interface and before shipping it was only $39.95 at [Newegg.com]("http://www.newegg.com").  

Trust me, it's worth the $$ to get hardware that works.  :)

Good luck!

### Post by Endolith on 2009-02-02
> **Bao2 said:**
> I would like download the .iso image, burn it to a CD and also let the .iso image in my secondary disk. 
Then boot the computer in the CD and then be able to continue installing using the CD or using the image .iso in my secondary disk. This way, choosing continuing the installation using the .iso image would be muuuuuuuuuch faster than installing from the CD in my opinion. Perhaps half the time?


[LIST]
[*] You can [upgrade]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/IntrepidUpgrades#Upgrading%20Using%20the%20Alternate%20CD/DVD") from an ISO
[*] You can [install from an ISO file on its own partition]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=4127061"), but it's a lot more work.
[*] Also, Knoppix has an option like [bootfrom=/dev/hda1/KNX.iso]("http://www.knoppix.net/wiki/Cheat_Codes")
[*] GRUB4DOS, GRUB? and GRUB 2 can supposedly boot from an ISO, though instructions are sketchy: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=774539](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=774539) [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=345212](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=345212) [http://mgerards.net/blog/?p=16](http://mgerards.net/blog/?p=16)
[/LIST]

### Post by xfred on 2009-02-02
Fresh install.

Positives:
- initial installation was relatively painless.
- dual screens now work properly.  With my last install the best I could manage on this box (dell, borderline unsupported hardware) was a kludge that wouldn't let me drag stuff from one screen to the other.  I was also very happy to find that I could finally set up dual-screen without resorting to xorg.conf, as is usually required.
- printer support seems to have improved significantly.

Negatives:
- Fonts.  When I first installed the fonts were hideous to the point of making me want to give up and load windows.  After much time and tweaking the fonts no longer make me want to puke, but they're still pretty bloody awful.  It probably doesn't help that msttcorefonts just plain will not install no matter what I try (I've basically given up).
- Screen setup gui: while I was impressed that it let me set up dual-screen without messing with my xorg.conf file, the process was still a little odd.  For example, available options for screen resolutions changed from boot to boot in a rather confusing manner.
- For some reason Kile has developed a habit of occasionally quitting mid-save, trashing documents in the process.  Not fun.

Overall: impressive and worth the effort, but not perfect.

---

### Post by solwic on 2009-02-02
> **xfred said:**
> Fresh install.

Negatives:
- Fonts.  When I first installed the fonts were hideous to the point of making me want to give up and load windows.  After much time and tweaking the fonts no longer make me want to puke, but they're still pretty bloody awful.  It probably doesn't help that msttcorefonts just plain will not install no matter what I try (I've basically given up).


Seriously?  You'd judge an entire OS by its fonts?  That's harsh.

msttcorefonts always gets installed for me when I run (at least I *think* it does) ```
 sudo apt-get install ubuntu-restricted-extras 
```  

Don't know if you want that whole package or not, or if you've done it yet, but it always works for me, and I don't see how hardware would limit what fonts you use, so you're either using 64bit or are doing something wrong.  :(

Good luck, if you keep trying.

---

### Post by frodon on 2009-03-03
The CPU thing has always existed as far as i remember and i never bothered with this neither been worried about it since i started using skype under linux 4 years ago.
About the sound it is just skype configuration issue, which is time consuming to solve i have to concede.

I believe i had to almost test all of them once to figure out the right option to choose for sound output to get what i want. Don't forget to check all volume levels in in the sound applet (the one in notification area), some of them are muted by default and i had to unmute them to get sound with skype.

Good luck.

It didn't, not for me anyway.

If I selected "use continuous free space" then the "after" graphic showed ubuntu using up 100% of my HD. (eek!)

1. Choose free space
2. Make partition
3. Choose partition
4. Install on chosen partition

### Post by jenkinbr on 2009-03-20
> **xyepblra said:**
> ...and rar/unrar function was not included into this distro, but the rest so far is close to perfect!

Rar is in multiverse, software with distribution issues goes here.
Install the rar and unrar packages from synaptic or at the command line.

sudo apt-get install rar unrar
